Proof from the Prophet's Sudden Eloquence
Argument from the Prophet's sudden eloquence as a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's sudden ability to produce unmatched eloquent speech without prior training is considered a definitive proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sudden, perfect eloquence—unprecedented in his life—is a clear miracle.

This passage presents the second of four types of miracles relating to the Prophet's personal condition. The author argues that the Prophet was not known for eloquence before his prophethood; then suddenly he produced speech that challenged the entire world. This abrupt transformation from silence to mastery is a sign of divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument come through.
Notice the logical structure: premise (no prior eloquence) → consequence (would have been known) → principle (not in human nature) → conclusion (miracle).
2
Identify the core argument
The passage argues that the Prophet's eloquence is miraculous because it appeared suddenly without any prior training or practice.
The key phrase is 'فجأة بلا مقدمة' (suddenly without foundation).
3
Consider the principle about human nature
The author states that it is not in human nature to suddenly produce speech that incapacitates others without gradual preparation. This principle supports the miraculous nature.
Why would gradual preparation matter? It shows that human achievement requires time and effort.
4
Reflect on the implications
If the Prophet could do what humans cannot do naturally, his claim of prophethood is supported. This is a rational argument for the truth of his message.
Compare with other miracles: they all exceed human capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: أنه لم يكن قبل إظهار الدعوة متكلما لما أظهره، ولا خائضا نظم الكلام وتأليفه، ولو كان شرع في شيء من ذلك لظهر لمعاشريه ولما خفى على أهل بطانته، وليس من طباع البشر التصدي لمثل ذلك الخطب الجليل والتعرض لمخالفة العالم فجأة بلا مقدمة ولا القدرة على الإتيان بكلام يعجز عنه الخلق بغتة من غير تدريج
And the second: that he was not before the proclamation of the call a speaker of what he brought, nor one who engaged in the composition and arrangement of speech. And had he embarked upon anything of that, it would have appeared to his contemporaries and would not have been hidden from his close associates. And it is not in the nature of humans to undertake such a great matter and to expose oneself to opposing the world suddenly without any prior foundation, nor to have the ability to produce speech that incapacitates creation all at once without gradual preparation.
Source pages p. 727

Commentary
This passage presents the second of the four divisions of miracles relating to the Prophet's personal condition. The author argues that Muhammad (peace be upon him) was not a speaker of eloquent speech or a composer of fine discourse before he announced his prophethood. If he had practiced such rhetoric, his contemporaries would have known about it, especially his close companions. The author then states a general principle: it is not in human nature to suddenly master a great oration that challenges the entire world without any prior training, nor to produce speech that humans are incapable of imitating without gradual development. This sudden ability is thus a clear miracle proving his prophethood.

Key Terms
متكلما
نظم الكلام
الخُطْب الجليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that eloquence itself is not miraculous, as many poets were eloquent.
Correction: The miracle lies in the sudden appearance of perfect eloquence without any prior practice or training, which is against human nature.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden, unparalleled eloquence, which he had never before demonstrated, is a clear sign that he was supported by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
You claim to believe, but does your life reflect a response to this miracle? The next time you read the Qur'an, will you see it as a divine challenge to your soul or just as words? Write down a concrete change you will make today to live as if the Prophet's miracle is real and demanding a response.

The Illiteracy Argument for Prophethood
First proof: illiteracy and unreachable knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's illiteracy and his knowledge of the unseen, despite no teachers, serve as a miraculous proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's illiteracy and hidden knowledge prove his message is from Allah.

This lesson presents the first of several proofs for the Prophet's prophethood. The author argues that the Prophet's environment was isolated and uneducated, and he had no opportunity to learn from scholars, yet he knew detailed news of the past and future. This demonstrates divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage starts mid-sentence; the proof continues from the previous page.
2
Identify the key elements
The author lists several factors: the Prophet's illiteracy, his environment, his limited travel, the absence of teachers, and his knowledge of the unseen. Find each one in the text.
These are the building blocks of the argument.
3
Examine the Quranic citations
The author cites five Quranic verses to support the argument. Locate them in the translation and consider how each reinforces the point that the Prophet's knowledge could not have been acquired through normal means.
The verses include the mubahala challenge, declaration of unseen revelation, and statements about the Prophet's prior illiteracy.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Think about why the combination of illiteracy and knowledge of the unseen is compelling. How does this argument address doubts about divine revelation?
This proof was directed at the polytheists who knew the Prophet's background.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودراستها، وكانت بلدتهم في البراري لا يشهدها إلا الأعراب الأميون الذين كان الغالب عليهم الجهل ، ثم هو لم يغب عنهم إلا مدة يسيرة في سفره إلى الشام مع العير، ولم يغب عنهم، ولم يقدم عليهم مكة أحد من أحبار أهل الكتاب والعلماء بشرائع الأمم المتقدمة يختصه ممن هو دونه ويعتكف على تعريفه ما في الكتب السالفة، ثم إنه علم أنباء الغيب الذي لم يكن يعلمها هو ولا أحد من قومه، وبلغ في ذلك الثقة به والطمأنينة إليه إلى أن قال عند مجادلتهم إياه : تَعَالَوْا نَدْعُ أَبْنَاءَنَا وَأَبْنَاءَكُمْ ﴾ (٢) وقال تعالى: تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ مَا كُنتَ تَعْلَمُهَا أَنتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ ) (۳) ولم ينسبه أحد منهم إلى تعلم قد تفرد به وأنفق عمره في تحصيله، وقال تعالى: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ مُنكَرُونَ ) () وقال : ( وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُوا مِن قَبْلِهِ، مِن كِتَبٍ وَلَا تَعْتُهُ ينِكَ إِذَا لَارْتابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ ) (۱) وقال : ( فَقَدْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ هُمُرًا مِّن قَبْلِهِ، أَفَلَا تعقلون
And his study of it, and his town was in the wilderness, visited only by Bedouin illiterates among whom ignorance prevailed, then he was not absent from them except for a short period in his journey to Syria with the caravan, and he was not absent from them, and no one of the rabbis of the People of the Book and scholars of the laws of previous nations came to them in Mecca to single him out from those below him and devote himself to teaching him what is in the previous books, then he knew the news of the unseen which he himself and none of his people knew, and he reached in that confidence and reassurance to the point that he said during their disputation with him: 'Come, let us call our sons and your sons' (2), and He said: 'That is from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know it, nor your people' (3), and none of them attributed to him that he had learned something unique and spent his life in acquiring it, and He said: 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' (5) and He said: 'And you did not recite before it any book, nor did you write it with your right hand; then the followers of falsehood would have doubted' (1), and He said: 'Indeed I have remained among you a lifetime before it; do you not then understand?'
Source pages p. 727

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof of the Prophet's prophethood: his illiteracy and his knowledge of the unseen despite the absence of any teacher. The author argues that the Prophet's environment was isolated and ignorant, and he was only briefly absent on a trade journey to Syria. No learned rabbis or scholars visited Mecca to teach him. Yet he accurately reported news of past scriptures and future events. The author cites several Quranic verses: the challenge of mutual imprecation (mubahala) in Surah Aal Imran, the declaration that the Quran is from the unseen in Surah Hud, the denial of the polytheists despite knowing him in Surah al-Mu'minoon, the fact that he was not previously a reciter or writer in Surah al-Ankabut, and his long known life among them in Surah Yunus. These collectively demonstrate that his knowledge could not have been acquired through ordinary means, thus proving divine revelation.

Key Terms
أمية (illiteracy)
أنباء الغيب (news of the unseen)
معرفة (knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic knowledge can be acquired through effort and study.
Correction: The passage shows the Prophet was illiterate, had no teachers, and lived in an ignorant environment, yet he knew details of previous scriptures and future events, indicating divine revelation.

Second Proof: Sudden Eloquence Without Prior Study
Second proof: sudden eloquence as a miracle without prior practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's sudden eloquence, without prior practice, serves as a proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
Sudden eloquence without prior study is a divine sign.

The second proof for prophethood focuses on the miraculous nature of the Quranic discourse. The Prophet, known for his honesty but not for eloquence, suddenly produced speech that challenges all creation. This lesson examines the logical argument that such a feat could only come from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Observe how the author sets up the argument: the Prophet had no prior practice in rhetoric.
2
Identify the key premise
The Prophet was not known for composing eloquent speech. If he had practiced, his contemporaries would have known.
3
Understand the conclusion
The sudden appearance of inimitable speech proves divine intervention. It is not in human nature to produce such a challenge without gradual preparation.
4
Reflect on the miracle
Contrast this with other miracles. The Quran itself is the miracle of eloquence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: أنه لم يكن قبل إظهار الدعوة متكلما لما أظهره، ولا خائضًا نظم الكلام وتأليفه، ولو كان شرع في شيء من ذلك لظهر لمعاشريه ولما خفى على أهل بطانته، وليس من طباع البشر التصدي لمثل ذلك الخطب الجليل والتعرض لمخالفة العالم فجأة بلا مقدمة ولا القدرة على الإتيان بكلام يعجز عنه الخلق بغتة من غير تدريج
And the second: that he was not before the announcement of the call a speaker of what he manifested, nor one plunging into the composition and arrangement of speech, and had he embarked on any of that, it would have appeared to his contemporaries and would not have been hidden from those close to him, and it is not in human nature to undertake such a great matter and to expose oneself to contradicting the world suddenly without introduction, nor the ability to produce speech that the creation is incapable of all at once without gradualness.
Source pages p. 727

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof: the Prophet's sudden eloquence. The author argues that before his public call, the Prophet was not known for engaging in rhetoric or composing eloquent speech. If he had practiced, his contemporaries would have known. But suddenly, he produced the Quranic discourse that challenges all mankind. This is not humanly possible without divine assistance.

Proof from Opposition Despite Weakness
Sanusi presents the third proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third rational proof for prophethood: that the Prophet's opposition to the entire world while in a state of weakness, and his ultimate success, could only be achieved through divine assistance.

Core Idea
Weakness plus total opposition plus success equals divine support.

The third proof for the prophethood of Muhammad ﷺ focuses on the extraordinary nature of his mission. He stood alone against the whole world, lacking wealth, allies, and power, yet he prevailed. This lesson unpacks that argument, showing why his success points directly to supernatural aid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and the translation. Notice the contrast between the Prophet's state (weak, poor, few helpers) and the magnitude of his opposition (all people, kings, tyrants).
Pay attention to the phrase 'war against all the people of the earth.'
2
Identify the core argument
The proof has three parts: 1) the Prophet's complete weakness, 2) his total opposition without compromise, and 3) the astonishing growth of his mission despite the full force of his enemies. Pinpoint each part in the text.
The enemies used every effort to extinguish his light, but only increased his followers.
3
Contrast with worldly kingdoms
Notice how the author contrasts the Prophet's situation with that of worldly rulers who rely on wealth and armies. This highlights the supernatural element.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that this can only be explained by divine assistance. The clue of being feared from a month's distance (terror) reinforces the miraculous nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث : أنه انتصب في حال ضعفه وفقره وفاقته وقلة أعوانه حربًا لجميع أهل الأرض ومتعرضا للملوك والجبارين وذوي القدرة والبسطة، وعاداهم معاداة الدين، وهي أشد أنواع العداوة، وسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يعتادون التفاخر بمآثرهم ومناقبهم ، وكان أشد الناس عليه عشيرته الأقربون ورهطه الأدنون، ولم يأخذه في الله لومة لائم، وطلبوا منه أدنى مداهنة ليتابعوه وأيسر مسايلة لينقادوا له، فلم يعطهم ذلك ولم يساعدهم عليه، ثم إنهم مع قوة أبدانهم وكثرة عدوهم ووفور عدوهم أتوا بأقصى ما في وسعهم من الجد والاجتهاد واستعمال العدة والعتاد لإطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره فلم يزدد ذلك إلا كثرة الأتباع وقوة الأشياع وانتشار الدعوة وشد الشوكة من غير أن كان ذلك راجعا إلى معونة بشرية على ما عليه أمر طلاب دول الدنيا المعتمدين في ذلك على كثرة الأموال وقوة الأنصار والأعوان، بل كان نشأ يتيمًا لا تبع له وعائلاً لا مال له، وهذا من أول الدلائل على أن أمره كان مبنيًا على المعونة الإلهية والتأييد السماوي، ولهذا بالرعب وكان يُخاف منه مسيرة شهر.
And the third: that he stood up in his state of weakness, poverty, need, and fewness of helpers as a war against all the people of the earth, exposing himself to kings, tyrants, and those of power and affluence, and he opposed them with the enmity of religion, which is the most severe type of enmity, and he belittled their intellects and the intellects of their fathers who used to boast of their exploits and merits, and the most severe of people against him were his nearest relatives and his closest clan, and no blame of a blamer affected him in [the cause of] Allah, and they asked him for the slightest compromise so that they might follow him and the easiest concession so that they might submit to him, but he did not give them that nor did he assist them in it, then they, with the strength of their bodies and the abundance of their numbers and the abundance of their enmity, brought the utmost of their effort and striving and use of equipment and armaments to extinguish his light and obliterate his traces, but that only increased the multitude of followers, the strength of the partisans, the spread of the call, and the solidity of the thorns, without that being due to human assistance in the manner of those who seek worldly kingdoms relying in that on abundance of wealth and strength of supporters and helpers, but rather he grew up an orphan with no followers and a dependant with no wealth, and this is among the first signs that his matter was based on divine assistance and heavenly support, and for this he was supported with terror and he was feared from a month's journey.
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof: the Prophet's unprecedented opposition to the world despite his extreme weakness. He challenged kings and tyrants, and his own closest relatives were his fiercest enemies. They offered him opportunities to compromise, but he refused steadfastly. Despite their full force, his movement only grew, and this growth was not through human means such as wealth or armies, as worldly rulers do. He started as an orphan with no following and no wealth. Therefore, his success must have come from divine support. The author notes that he was aided by terror (being feared from a month's distance) as a clear supernatural sign.

Key Terms
ضعف
معونة إلهية
رعب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some attribute the Prophet's success to political strategy or military power.
Correction: The proof shows the Prophet had no wealth, army, or helpers initially, yet succeeded against all odds, indicating divine rather than human means.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, what indicates that the Prophet's success was divine?
A) His wealth and powerful allies.
B) His opposition to the world despite weakness and poverty, yet he prevailed without human support.
C) The weakness of his enemies.
D) His gradual compromise with opponents.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's overwhelming success from a position of extreme weakness proves his prophethood and divine backing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The proof shows that true success comes from divine support, not human resources. Are you relying more on your own plans, wealth, or connections than on Allah? What is one concrete step you can take this week to shift your trust from your own means to Allah's help?

Fourth Proof: The Prophet's Steadfastness and Patience
Sanusi presents the fourth proof: the Prophet's steadfastness despite hardships and temptations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's extraordinary steadfastness and refusal of worldly temptations serve as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's refusal of wealth and power proves his mission is from God.

This lesson examines the fourth proof from classical kalam: the Prophet's unmatched patience and persistence in delivering his message despite severe hardships. Sanusi argues that such steadfastness, combined with his rejection of worldly offers, cannot be explained by human ambition alone. The passage highlights the Prophet's unwavering dedication as a sign of divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice how the proof is built on two key observations: the Prophet's endurance of hardship and his refusal of temptations.
The passage ends midway; the argument is still clear.
2
Identify the three components of the proof
List: 1) Hardships borne that are beyond human capacity. 2) His constancy without fatigue. 3) His rejection of offers of wealth and leadership.
3
Understand the logical connection
Ask yourself: why does this combination of hardship and refusal point to truthfulness? Because a false prophet would have accepted worldly gain. The Prophet's behavior is inconsistent with seeking personal benefit.
This reasoning is central to the proof.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider how this proof appeals to common human psychology: anyone enduring such difficulty must have a deep conviction.
This proof complements the earlier proofs by addressing character and motivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرابع أنه عليه السلام تحمل في إظهار دعوته المشاق التي لا خفاء بمكانها، والمتاعب التي ليست في الجملة البشرية احتمالها فدام في ذلك كله على وتيرة واحدة لا يسأم عن شأنه ولا يمل عن دعوته، وعرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليترك دعوته فلم يجبهم إلى ذلك بل قال : وَمَا أَسْلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ ) ( وصبر على تلك المشاقات مترددًا في البؤس والفاقة منصرفًا في الضراء واللداء

Commentary

He was offered wealth and leadership to stop his call, but he refused, citing that he asks no reward. His patience in poverty and adversity demonstrates that he was not after worldly gain, but his mission was from God. The passage ends abruptly, but the argument is clear.

The Third Proof: Weakness and Divine Support
Imam Nasafi presents the third proof of prophethood: the Prophet's weakness and divine support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof of prophethood, which argues that the Prophet's triumph despite his initial weakness and the full force of his enemies demonstrates divine support, not human means.

Core Idea
The Prophet's victory from a state of weakness proves Allah's direct support.

Imam Nasafi presents a compelling proof: how could an orphan with no resources challenge the world's powers and win? The answer is divine assistance. This passage examines the argument that the Prophet's extraordinary success despite overwhelming odds is a clear sign of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic source and its literal translation. Try to grasp the overall argument before analyzing details.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the key contrast
Notice the contrast between the Prophet's weakness (poverty, lack of supporters) and the power of his enemies (kings, tyrants, abundance). Ask yourself: how could such a weak person succeed?
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that the Prophet's success came from divine support and heavenly assistance. Recognize that the proof hinges on the impossibility of human explanation.
This connects to the concept of 'awe' (رعب) as a sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث : أنه انتصب في حال ضعفه وفقره وفاقته وقلة أعوانه حربًا لجميع أهل الأرض ومتعرضا للملوك والجبارين وذوي القدرة والبسطة(۱)، وعاداهم معاداة الدين، وهي أشد أنواع العداوة، وسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يعتادون التفاخر بمآثرهم ومناقبهم ، وكان أشد الناس عليه عشيرته الأقربون ورهطه الأدنون، ولم يأخذه في الله لومة لائم، وطلبوا منه أدنى مداهنة ليتابعوه (۲) وأيسر مسايلة لينقادوا له، فلم يعطهم ذلك ولم يساعدهم عليه، ثم إنهم مع قوة أبدانهم وكثرة عدوهم ووفور عدوهم أتوا بأقصى ما في وسعهم من الجد والاجتهاد واستعمال العدة والعتاد لإطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره فلم يزدد ذلك إلا كثرة الأتباع وقوة الأشياع وانتشار الدعوة وشد الشوكة من غير أن كان ذلك راجعا إلى(۳) معونة بشرية على ما عليه أمر طلاب دول الدنيا المعتمدين في ذلك على كثرة الأموال وقوة الأنصار والأعوان، بل كان نشأ يتيمًا لا تبع له وعائلاً لا مال له، وهذا من أول الدلائل على أن أمره كان مبنيًا على المعونة الإلهية والتأييد السماوي، ولهذا بالرعب وكان يُخاف منه مسيرة شهر.
And the third: that he stood up in his state of weakness, poverty, need, and fewness of supporters as a war against all the people of the earth, exposing himself to kings, tyrants, and those of power and authority. He enmity them with the enmity of religion, which is the severest kind of enmity, and he regarded their minds and the minds of their fathers, who were accustomed to boast of their exploits and merits, as foolish. And the most severe of people against him were his nearest kin and his closest tribe. He did not fear the blame of any blamer for the sake of God. They asked from him the slightest compromise so that they would follow him, and the easiest concession so that they would submit to him, but he did not give them that and did not help them in it. Then they, with the strength of their bodies, the multitude of their enemies (?), and the abundance of their enemies (?) came with the utmost of their effort and exertion, using weaponry and equipment to extinguish his light and obliterate his traces, but that only increased the multitude of followers, the strength of partisans, the spread of the call, and the firmness of his power, without that being due to human assistance, as is the case with the seekers of worldly kingdoms who rely in that on abundance of wealth and strength of supporters and helpers. Rather, he grew up as an orphan with no follower and a dependent with no wealth. This is among the first proofs that his affair was based on divine assistance and heavenly support, and for this reason he was supported by awe and was feared for a month's journey.
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof of the Prophet's prophethood. The argument is that despite the Prophet's state of extreme weakness, poverty, and lack of supporters, he challenged the entire world—kings and tyrants—with the enmity of religion. His own tribe and relatives were his harshest opponents. They sought the slightest compromise, but he refused. In response, they used all their power and resources to extinguish his message, yet this only increased his followers and strengthened his mission. This success was not due to human support—he was an orphan with no wealth or followers—so it must be from divine assistance. The proof ends by noting that he was granted awe (رعب) such that he was feared from a month's distance. The author argues that this is a clear sign that his mission was divinely supported.

Nasafi argues from the Prophet's consistent behavior in hardship and success.

By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's consistency in both adversity and success proves his prophethood.

Core Idea
Consistency in both hardship and ease proves the Prophet's sincerity.

Imam Nasafi now presents the fourth proof: the Prophet's remarkable perseverance in the face of extreme hardship, and his equally remarkable refusal to change his ascetic lifestyle after triumph. This consistency is a powerful sign that his actions were not driven by worldly ambition, but by divine mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

This is the core of the proof.
3
Reflect on the conclusion

This ties worldly behavior to the afterlife.

And the fourth: that he, peace be upon him, bore in the manifestation of his call the hardships whose places are not hidden, and the troubles that the human capacity cannot bear. He continued in all that on one steady path, not wearied of his matter nor bored of his call. Worldly desires of wealth and leadership were presented to him to abandon his call, but he did not respond to them; rather, he said: 'I do not ask you for any reward for it.' He persevered through those hardships, moving about in misery and poverty, enduring adversity and affliction, patient on the hardship of life. Then when matters became rectified for him, the public submitted to his call, the delegations of Arabs from plain and mountain struck at his door with the humps of camels, abundant wealth and precious necklaces were brought to him, the Arabian Peninsula became serene for him entirely, cleared of those who opposed him and devoid of those who contended and resisted him within it, he continued on his path and persisted in adhering to his way, abandoning the enjoyment of varieties of sensual pleasures and turning away from what is the habit of seekers of kingship: the acquisition of worldly blessings. Rather, he remained patient on what he had been in of humility, lowliness, and gulping the bitterness of poverty and need. And do not imagine that without sincere insight and complete trust in his Lord; rather, all of that was because Allah honored him and created him for the abode of His generosity which is prepared for blessings that are not disturbed by fear of cessation and not spoilt by the admixture of demand. And Allah is the possessor of favor and bounty.
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof of the Prophet's prophethood. The author argues that the Prophet endured unbearable hardships while spreading his message without tiring. He rejected offers of wealth and leadership to abandon his call, as stated in the Quran. Then, after he achieved total success and all of Arabia submitted to him, he did not change his lifestyle: he continued to avoid worldly pleasures and preserved his asceticism. This consistency shows that his actions were not motivated by worldly ambition. The author concludes that this could only be due to sincere insight and trust in God, and that he was prepared for the eternal blessings of the next life. This argument highlights the Prophet's sincerity and divine mission.

Key Terms
الوتيرة (steady path)
التباؤس (humility)
دار الكرامة (abode of generosity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is about the Prophet's poverty or that he never possessed wealth.
Correction: The proof is not about poverty per se, but about his refusal to change his ascetic lifestyle after gaining power and wealth. He had access to riches but chose to remain humble.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth proof emphasize about the Prophet after his conquest of Arabia?
A) He began to enjoy worldly pleasures.
B) He continued his ascetic lifestyle unchanged.
C) He increased his wealth.
D) He became a tyrant.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof shows that the Prophet's unwavering consistency in both suffering and success confirms his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve success or gain something you desired, do your priorities shift away from Allah? The Prophet did not change. Are you honest enough to examine if your worship increases or decreases with your circumstances?
?
Wealth and power were offered to the Prophet to abandon his call. What are the 'wealth and power' offered to you in your life that tempt you to soften your commitment to Islam? Will you say 'I do not ask for any reward' as the Prophet did?
?
The Prophet remained patient in extreme hardship and then in success. Which situation is harder for you to maintain your deen: when you are suffering or when you are comfortable? What concrete step will you take this week to ensure consistency?

The Proof from the Prophet's Noble Lineage
Nasafi presents the lineage-based proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad's lineage serves as a proof of his prophethood by fulfilling Abraham's prayer.

Core Idea
The Prophet's lineage proves him as the answer to Abraham's prayer.

Imam Nasafi presents a unique proof of prophethood rooted in the Quran itself. He shows that the Prophet Muhammad is the direct fulfillment of Abraham's supplication for a messenger from his descendants through Ishmael. By examining the Prophet's noble lineage and the absence of any other prophet from Ishmael's line, Nasafi solidifies this argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Quranic basis
Read the verse quoted from Surah al-Baqara where Abraham prays for a messenger from his descendants. Note that the context is about Ishmael's line.
The verse is partially quoted; you may consult the full Quranic context.
2
Identify the connection to the Prophet
The author states that the Prophet is that answered prayer. Ask: Why is this specific to Muhammad? Because he is the only prophet from the children of Ishmael.
3
Examine the lineage list
Read the list of ancestors from Ishmael to 'Abd al-Muttalib. This lineage establishes his descent from Abraham through Ishmael.
The list includes famous ancestors like Ma'ad, Mudar, etc.
4
Reflect on the proof structure
Notice that the proof has two parts: the prophetic sign (fulfillment of prayer) and the historical verification (genealogy). Both work together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى نسبه عليه السلام فإنه كان دعوة إبراهيم عليه السلام على ما أخبر الله خبرًا عن إبراهيم أنه قال: رَبَّنَا وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُمْ ) والهاء عائدة إلى ذريته وذرية إسماعيل عليه السلام فإن في صدر الآية: ﴿وَإِذْ يَرْفَعُ إِبْرَاهِيمُ الْقَوَاعِدَ مِنَ الْبَيْتِ إلى أن قال : وَاجْعَلْنَا مُسْلِمَيْنِ لَكَ وَمِن ذُرِّيَّتِنَا أُمَّةً مُّسْلِمَةٌ لَكَ ثم قال وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُم ) ولا نبي من ولد إسماعيل عليه السلام إلا نبينا محمد سيد البشر ، ثم إنه عليه السلام كان حفدة إسماعيل، ونجل معد بن عدنان ونجيب مدر بن نذار، وسليل النضر بن كتانة، وأورع بني لؤي بن غالب، ولباب قصي بن كلاب، وصريح عبد مناف، وصفوة عمرو العلي وهو هاشم، وخلاصة عبد المطلب
And as for what relates to his noble lineage, peace be upon him: it is that he was the prayer of Abraham, peace be upon him, as God told us about Abraham that he said: 'Our Lord, raise up among them a messenger from among them.' The pronoun refers to his descendants and the descendants of Ishmael, peace be upon him. For at the beginning of the verse: 'And when Abraham was raising the foundations of the House' until he said: 'And make us both submitters to You, and from our descendants a submitting nation to You'; then he said 'And raise up among them a messenger from among them.' And there is no prophet from the children of Ishmael except our Prophet Muhammad, the master of mankind. Then, he, peace be upon him, was the grandson of Ishmael, the son of Ma'ad ibn 'Adnan, the noble of Mudar ibn Nizar, the descendant of al-Nadr ibn Kinana, the most pious of Banu Lu'ay ibn Ghalib, the core of Qusayy ibn Kilab, the pure of 'Abd Manaf, the chosen of 'Amr al-'Ala who is Hashim, and the cream of 'Abd al-Muttalib.
Source pages p. 729

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of the Prophet's prophethood based on his lineage. The author argues that the Prophet Muhammad is the fulfillment of Abraham's prayer in the Quran (Surah al-Baqara, verse 129) asking God to raise a messenger among the descendants of Ishmael. Since no other prophet came from Ishmael's line, Muhammad is that messenger. The author then lists the Prophet's noble lineage from Ishmael to 'Abd al-Muttalib, emphasizing his prestigious ancestry. This lineage proves he is the expected prophet.

Key Terms
نسب (lineage)
دعوة إبراهيم (prayer of Abraham)
ذرية إسماعيل (descendants of Ishmael)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof from lineage is merely about the Prophet's noble birth and honor.
Correction: The primary significance is that his lineage fulfills a specific prayer of Abraham, making it a prophetic sign, not just a mark of honor.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what makes the Prophet's lineage a proof of his prophethood?
A) He was from the richest tribe.
B) He is the only prophet from the descendants of Ishmael, fulfilling Abraham's prayer.
C) He was a descendant of Abraham through Isaac.
D) His lineage is traceable to all previous prophets.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's lineage proves his prophethood because he is the sole prophet from the descendants of Ishmael, fulfilling Abraham's prayer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abraham prayed for a messenger to guide his descendants, and that prayer was answered with Muhammad. You are among those who claim to follow that messenger. Are you living in a way that honors Abraham's prayer? What is one specific change you can make today to be a better follower of the messenger Abraham asked for?
?
The Prophet's lineage is traced through generations of pious ancestors, each described with noble traits. If your spiritual lineage were traced back to the Prophet, what traits would be listed about you? Are you proud of what that lineage would show?
?
If Muhammad is the answer to Abraham's prayer, then every moment you spend neglecting his teachings is a moment of ingratitude for that answered prayer. What will you do today to show that you truly value this gift?

The Prophet's Steadfastness and Asceticism After Gaining Power
Al-Nasafi describes the Prophet's continued simplicity and patience despite worldly success.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi presents the Prophet's voluntary asceticism after gaining worldly power as evidence of his sincerity and complete trust in God.

Core Idea
The Prophet's simplicity after success proves his sincerity and trust in God.

Al-Nasafi provides a moving description of the Prophet's character: he remained patient through hardship and, even after achieving political and spiritual dominance, continued to live simply, avoiding wealth and luxury. This lesson explores that description and its deeper significance, showing how the Prophet's behavior was not out of necessity but from profound spiritual insight and trust in God. You will see how al-Nasafi uses this to underscore the Prophet's unique status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage slowly
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the contrast al-Nasafi builds between the early hardship and later success, and then the surprising continuation of simplicity.
Pay attention to the words for hardship and success.
2
Identify the three phases
Identify the three phases: initial hardship, later success with resources, and the Prophet's unchanged asceticism. See how al-Nasafi transitions between them.
3
Understand the explanation
Al-Nasafi then gives the reason: the Prophet's behavior stems from true insight and complete trust in God, not from lack of opportunity. Grasp how he turns an observation into a theological point.
This connects the Prophet's actions to his prophethood.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Consider the misconception that the Prophet's later wealth (the gifts and tribute) contradicts his early poverty. Al-Nasafi's passage directly addresses this by showing that wealth was available but he chose simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صابرًا على شظف العيش ، ثم لما استقامت له الأمور وخضعت لدعوته الجمهور وضربت وفود العرب من السهل والجبل إلى بابه أكباد الأبل، وحملت إليه الأموال الجمة والعقد النفيسة، وصفت له جزيرة العرب بأسرها وخلصت عمن يعاديه وخلت عمن ينازعه ويناوئه فيها ، استمر على وتيرته، وداوم على التمسك بطريقته من ترك الاستمتاع بصنوف الملاذ الشهوية والإعراض عما هو دأب طلاب الملك من إحراز النعم الدنيوية، بل صبر على ما كان عليه من التباؤس والاستكانة والتجرع لمضض الفقر والفاقة، ولا يتوهم ذلك بلا بصيرة صادقة وثقة بربه تامة بل كل ذلك لما أكرمه الله تعالى وخلقه لدار كرامته التي أعدت للنعم التي لا يكدرها خوف الزوال ولا ينغصها شوب المطال، والله ذو المن والإفضال.
He was patient on the hardship of living, then when affairs became steady for him and the masses submitted to his call and the delegations of Arabs from the plain and mountain struck the livers of camels to his door, and abundant wealth and precious necklaces were brought to him, and the whole Arabian Peninsula became clear for him, purified from those who opposed him and empty of those who contended with him in it, he continued on his course and persisted in adhering to his way: abandoning enjoyment of the varied kinds of sensory pleasures and turning away from what is the habit of seekers of kingship in acquiring worldly blessings. Rather, he remained patient on what he was upon of destitution and humility and swallowing the bitterness of poverty and need. And let no one imagine that that was without true insight and complete trust in his Lord. Rather, all that was because God Almighty honored him and created him for the abode of His generosity which is prepared for blessings that are not disturbed by fear of vanishing nor spoiled by the admixture of demands. And God is the Possessor of bounty and favor.
Source pages p. 729

Commentary
This passage is a description of the Prophet Muhammad's character, specifically his steadfastness in asceticism and simplicity even after achieving worldly power and success. The author al-Nasafi first describes the Prophet's initial state: he was patient with a harsh life. Then, as his mission succeeded, people submitted, delegations came from far and wide bearing gifts, and all of Arabia was under his control. Yet, al-Nasafi emphasizes that the Prophet did not change: he continued his previous simple way, avoiding sensory pleasures and worldly accumulation. Instead, he remained in a state of humility and poverty. Al-Nasafi then argues that this behavior cannot be without true spiritual insight and complete trust in God; rather, it is because God honored him and prepared him for an eternal abode of blessings that are imperishable. The passage concludes by attributing all this generosity to God.

Key Terms

استقامة الأمور
البصيرة الصادقة
الثقة بالله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Prophet's later wealth contradicted his early poverty.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that the Prophet voluntarily continued his asceticism despite having access to wealth, proving it was a deliberate spiritual choice.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Nasafi highlight the Prophet's continued simplicity after gaining power?
A) To show that prophethood requires poverty
B) To demonstrate his sincerity and trust in God
C) To argue that wealth is forbidden for prophets
D) To criticize the companions

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's voluntary asceticism after worldly success proves his sincerity and complete trust in God, not necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have successes too – a good job, a family, respect. Do you become more attached to these comforts, or do you find yourself increasingly detached, like the Prophet? What would it cost you to truly trust God enough to let go of one of those comforts today?
?
The Prophet, after conquering Arabia, remained in 'destitution and humility'. When you gain power or influence, do you seek elevation or do you intentionally lower yourself? Name one concrete way you can practice humility this week.
?
Al-Nasafi says the Prophet's asceticism was because of 'true insight and complete trust' – he saw the hereafter as the real treasure. If you truly believed that the blessings of Paradise never vanish, what possession or position would you start loosening your grip on right now?

The Prophet's Lineage: A Proof of Truthfulness
Al-Nasafi details the Prophet's lineage from Abraham and Ishmael and argues that noble ancestry precludes falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi uses the Prophet's noble lineage as a rational proof of his prophethood, demonstrating that a person of such ancestry cannot be a liar or fabricator.

Core Idea
The Prophet's noble lineage is not just history—it is a proof of his truthfulness.

Al-Nasafi begins by connecting the Prophet Muhammad directly to the prayer of Abraham, establishing his prophethood from the Qur'an. He then traces the Prophet's genealogy through the noblest Arab tribes, showing that every ancestor was a leader and a paragon of virtue. The point is not merely biographical; it is theological: a person from such an exalted family could never be a fabricator. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Prophetic supplication
Read the opening lines where al-Nasafi cites Abraham's prayer. Notice that the Qur'anic verse is used to show that Muhammad is the answer to that prayer.
The pronoun 'them' refers to the descendants of Ishmael.
2
Trace the lineage
Follow the list of ancestors from Ishmael down to 'Abd al-Muttalib. See how each is described with superlative qualities like 'master,' 'pure,' 'essence.'
These titles emphasize unparalleled nobility.
3
Consider the maternal connections
Al-Nasafi also mentions the Prophet's noble lineage through mothers of his forefathers and his own mother, showing the breadth of his honorable descent.
4
Grasp the concluding argument
Read the final part where al-Nasafi states that such noble lineage makes it impossible for the Prophet to be a fabricator. Only a person of base origin would lie.
This is the key proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هم راجع إلى نسبه الشريف فإنه كان دعوة إبراهيم عليه السلام على ما أخبر الله خبرًا عن إبراهيم أنه قال: رَبَّنَا وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُمْ والهاء عائدة إلى ذريته وذرية إسماعيل عليه السلام فإن في صدر الآية: ﴿وَإِذْ يَرْفَعُ إِبْرَاهِمُ الْقَوَاعِدَ مِنَ الْبَيْتِ إلى أن قال : وَاجْعَلْنَا مُسْلِمَيْنِ لَكَ وَمِن ذُرِّيَّتِنَا أُمَّةً مُّسْلِمَةٌ لَكَ ثم قال وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُم ولا نبي من ولد إسماعيل عليه السلام إلا نبينا محمد سيد البشر ، ثم إنه عليه السلام كان حفدة إسماعيل، ونجل معد بن عدنان ونجيب مدر بن نذار، وسليل النضر بن كتانة، وأورع بني لؤي بن غالب، ولباب قصي بن كلاب، وصريح عبد مناف، وصفوة عمرو العلي وهو هاشم، وخلاصة عبد المطلب وهو شبيه الحمد ، و من قبل أمهات آبائه متصلاً بمضاض بن عمرو الجرهمي جد ذكورة ولد إسماعيل وبأخواله من الخزرج بسلمى والدة عبد المطلب وبني زهرة بأمه آمنة، وله عليه السلام أنساب شريفة من قبل أمهات آبائه كالعواتك والفواطم وغيرهن، ثم لا يخفى على العلماء بالتواريخ والحفاظ لأنساب العرب وأيامها العارفين بأشرافهم وأجوادهم وشجعانهم أن كل واحد ممن يتصل نسبه به، كان عمادًا لأسرته ورئيسًا لقبيلته وزمرته وسيدًا لعشيرته مخصوصا بجميع الفضائل موصوفًا بالمحامد والمناقب، وكانوا أرباب الحكم والرفادة، وأصحاب السقاية والسدانة، وسادة دار الندوة، والوافدين عند الملوك والأجلة المعظمين في أعينهم المتبجلين عندهم المسمين عند جميع قبائل العرب - قحطانها وعدنانها مضرها وربيعها قيسها وخندقها آل الله وجيرانه وسكان حرمه ومن كان حال نسبه هذه الحالة، وعرقه في الشرف هذا العرق كان الاشتغال منه بالرزق والافتعال من الممتنع الذي لا تصور له والمحال الذي لا مجال له في العقول لثبوته إذ ذلك فعل من يرجع إلى خساسة في الأصل وضعة في النسب ولؤم في الأعراق ودناءه في الأخلاق، وبالله التوفيق.
And as for what pertains to his noble lineage, he was the supplication of Abraham, peace be upon him, as God informed us about Abraham that he said: 'Our Lord, send among them a messenger from themselves'—the pronoun refers to his descendants and the descendants of Ishmael, peace be upon him. For in the beginning of the verse: 'And when Abraham was raising the foundations of the House' until he said: 'And make us submitters to You and from our descendants a nation submitting to You' then he said 'And send among them a messenger from themselves.' And there is no prophet from the children of Ishmael, peace be upon him, except our prophet Muhammad, the master of mankind. Then he, peace be upon him, was the grandson of Ishmael, the son of Ma'd ibn Adnan, the noble of Mudar ibn Nizar, the descendant of al-Nadr ibn Kinanah, the most pious of the sons of Lu'ayy ibn Ghalib, the core of Qusayy ibn Kilab, the pure of 'Abd Manaf, the elite of 'Amr al-'Ali who is Hashim, the essence of 'Abd al-Muttalib who is the likeness of praise. And on the side of the mothers of his forefathers, he is connected to Mudad ibn 'Amr al-Jurhumi, the grandfather of the males of the children of Ishmael, and through his maternal uncles from al-Khazraj through Sulma, the mother of 'Abd al-Muttalib, and through the Banu Zuhra through his mother Aminah. And he, peace be upon him, has noble lineages from the side of the mothers of his forefathers, such as al-'Awatik and al-Fawatim and others. Then it is not hidden from the scholars of histories and the memorizers of the genealogies of the Arabs and their days, those knowledgeable of their nobles, their generous, and their brave, that every one connected to him in lineage was a pillar for his family, a chief for his tribe and group, and a master for his clan, singled out with all virtues, described with praiseworthy qualities and merits. And they were the lords of judgment and support, the owners of giving drink and service, the masters of the house of counsel, and those who visited kings and great ones, honored in their eyes, esteemed before them, named among all the tribes of the Arabs—Qahtan and Adnan, Mudar and Rabi'ah, Qays and Khindif—as the family of God and His neighbors and the inhabitants of His sanctuary. And whoever's lineage is in this state, and whose root in nobility is this root, it is impossible for him to be occupied with seeking provision and fabrication; it is from the impossible that has no conception and the absurd that has no place in intellects due to its establishment. For that is the action of one who traces back to baseness in origin, lowliness in lineage, meanness in roots, and vileness in character. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 729

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Prophet Muhammad's noble lineage. Al-Nasafi begins by connecting him to the prayer of Abraham: Abraham asked God to send a messenger from among his descendants, and that messenger is Muhammad, as he is the only prophet from Ishmael's line. The author then lists the Prophet's ancestors from the most prominent Arab tribes, emphasizing their nobility: Ishmael, Ma'd ibn Adnan, Mudar, Nizar, Kinanah, Quraysh, and so on down to Hashim and 'Abd al-Muttalib. He also mentions the Prophet's connections through maternal lines to important families like al-Khazraj and Banu Zuhra. Al-Nasafi then argues that all these ancestors were leaders, generous, brave, and held high positions: they were the ones in charge of judgment, providing water, tending the Kaaba, and the council. They were honored by kings and tribes. Therefore, it is impossible that someone from such a noble lineage would be a liar or a fabricator; only one of base origin would do such things. This serves as a proof of the Prophet's truthfulness, as his noble descent is incompatible with falsehood.

Key Terms
نسب شريف
دعوة إبراهيم
حفدة إسماعيل
آل الله وجيرانه
خساسة الأصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's lineage is merely a historical curiosity.
Correction: Al-Nasafi uses it as a rational argument: a person from such an exalted family cannot be a liar, thus supporting his prophethood.

Checkpoint
How does al-Nasafi use the Prophet's lineage to support his prophethood?
A) By showing that all his ancestors were prophets
B) By arguing that a noble lineage precludes lying and fabrication
C) By proving he was descended from kings
D) By listing his wealth and power

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi argues that the Prophet's unparalleled noble lineage logically precludes him from being a fabricator, making his prophethood credible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the Prophet's noble lineage being used as proof of his truthfulness, how does that challenge you to examine the consistency between your own background and your words? Are you living up to the noble character of your spiritual lineage as a follower of Muhammad?
?
Al-Nasafi states that only a person of 'baseness in origin and vileness in character' would fabricate religious claims. Do you ever find yourself attributing things to God or His religion without sure knowledge? What steps will you take today to ensure your speech about Islam is always truthful and based on evidence?
?
If the Prophet's ancestors were described as 'pillars for their families' and 'masters for their clans,' what kind of legacy are you building in your own family and community? What can you change starting this week to become a 'pillar' for those around you?

The Prophet's Noble Lineage as Proof of Truthfulness
The author argues that the Prophet's noble lineage makes lying rationally impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's noble lineage serves as a rational proof of his truthfulness in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
A noble lineage makes falsehood rationally impossible.

The author presents a unique argument for the Prophet's truthfulness: his impeccable ancestry. By examining the noble qualities of his forebears, he concludes that lying is incompatible with such a lineage. This lesson explores how lineage serves as a corroborative proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to the lineage details mentioned.
The passage begins with 'وهو' referring to the Prophet from the previous page.
2
Identify the lineage details
Notice how the author traces the Prophet's lineage from both parents and mentions tribes and individuals like Mudad, Salma, and Banu Zuhra.
These details establish the nobility of his ancestry.
3
Understand the rational argument
The author argues that someone with such a lineage cannot engage in lying or base behavior, as that is characteristic of lowly origins.
Think about why this argument would be compelling in a pre-Islamic Arabian context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو شبيه الحمد ، و من قبل أمهات آبائه متصلاً بمضاض بن عمرو الجرهمي جد ذكورة ولد إسماعيل وبأخواله من الخزرج بسلمى والدة عبد المطلب وبني زهرة بأمه آمنة، وله عليه السلام أنساب شريفة من قبل أمهات آبائه كالعواتك والفواطم وغيرهن، ثم لا يخفى على العلماء بالتواريخ والحفاظ لأنساب العرب وأيامها العارفين بأشرافهم وأجوادهم وشجعانهم أن كل واحد ممن يتصل نسبه به، كان عمادًا لأسرته ورئيسًا لقبيلته وزمرته وسيدًا لعشيرته مخصوصا بجميع الفضائل موصوفًا بالمحامد والمناقب، وكانوا أرباب الحكم والرفادة، وأصحاب السقاية والسدانة، وسادة دار الندوة، والوافدين عند الملوك والأجلة المعظمين في أعينهم المتبجلين عندهم المسمين عند جميع قبائل العرب - قحطانها وعدنانها مضرها وربيعها قيسها وخندقها آل الله وجيرانه وسكان حرمه ومن كان حال نسبه هذه الحالة، وعرقه في الشرف هذا العرق كان الاشتغال منه بالرزق والافتعال من الممتنع الذي لا تصور له والمحال الذي لا مجال له في العقول لثبوته إذ ذلك فعل من يرجع إلى خساسة في الأصل وضعة في النسب ولؤم في الأعراق ودناءه في الأخلاق، وبالله التوفيق.
And he is the like of praise, and from the mothers of his fathers, connected to Mudad ibn Amr al-Jurhami, the grandfather of the male descendants of Ismail, and through his maternal uncles from Khazraj to Salma, the mother of Abd al-Muttalib, and to Banu Zuhra through his mother Amina. And he (peace be upon him) has noble lineages from the mothers of his fathers, such as al-Awatik and al-Fawatim and others. Then it is not hidden from scholars of histories and preservers of the genealogies of the Arabs and their days, those knowledgeable of their nobles, their generous ones, and their brave ones, that every one who is connected to him in lineage was a pillar for his family, a chief for his tribe and group, a lord for his clan, distinguished with all virtues, described with praise and merits. And they were lords of wisdom and support, owners of water-giving and guardianship, masters of the house of counsel, and those who visit kings and great ones, magnified in their eyes, venerated before them, renowned among all Arab tribes—Qahtan and Adnan, Mudar and Rabi'a, Qays and Khindif—people of God, neighbors of His sanctuary, inhabitants of His sacred precincts. And whoever's lineage is in this state, and his root in nobility is this root, then his occupation with livelihood and fabrication is impossible, inconceivable, and rationally impossible to affirm, for that is the action of one who goes back to baseness in origin, lowliness in lineage, meanness in roots, and lowness in character. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 730

Commentary
This passage provides a rational proof of prophethood based on the Prophet's noble lineage. The author first details the Prophet's impeccable ancestry from both his father's and mother's sides, mentioning prominent tribes and personalities. He then argues that anyone connected to such a lineage is naturally a leader and possesses noble qualities. Consequently, it is rationally impossible for a person with such a pure and noble lineage to engage in lying or seeking worldly gain, as such behavior is characteristic of those of base origin. Thus, the Prophet's truthfulness is supported by his lineage.

The Prophet's Supplication Against Mudar as a Miracle
The author recounts the answered supplication of the Prophet against Mudar as a proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's answered supplication against Mudar serves as a proof of prophethood, transmitted by mass narration.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer against Mudar was answered decisively, confirming his prophethood.

This lesson presents a powerful example of a prophetic miracle: the Prophet's supplication against the tribe of Mudar. When they harmed him, he prayed for a famine, and it came. Then he prayed for relief, and it came so abundantly that houses were destroyed. The author emphasizes that this event is transmitted by tawatur, making it an undeniable proof of prophethood. As you read the passage, note the direct cause-and-effect relationship between his prayer and the natural events.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the specific wording of the supplications and the sequence of events.
The passage is concise but packed with detail.
2
Identify the two supplications
Find where the Prophet makes his first supplication against Mudar and the second supplication when they asked for relief. Note the outcomes of each.
The first prays for punishment, the second for relief.
3
Understand the significance of tawatur
The passage ends by stating that all of this is transmitted by tawatur (mass transmission). Ask yourself why the author emphasizes this point.
Tawatur makes the report certain and irrefutable.
4
Reflect on the miracle as proof
Consider how this event demonstrates the Prophet's connection to Allah. His supplication was answered precisely, showing that he speaks with divine authority.
This is a direct proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن ذلك دعاؤه على مضر حين آذوه وكذبوه فقال : اللهم أشدد وطأتك على مضر، واجعل عليهم سنين كسني يوسف فأمسك عنهم القطر حتى جف النبات والشجر وهلكت المواشي. وكان انكشاف الجدب عنهم أيضًا بدعائه فأتاهم الغيث وكثر حتى هدم بيوتهم فكلموه في ذلك فقال : اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا، اللهم على الظراب والجبال وبطون الأودية وذلك كله منقول بالتواتر.
Among that is his supplication against Mudar when they harmed him and denied him, so he said: 'O God, make Your punishment severe upon Mudar, and give them years like the years of Joseph.' Then He withheld rain from them until plants and trees dried up and livestock perished. And the removal of drought from them was also by his supplication, so rain came to them and increased until it destroyed their houses. They spoke to him about that, so he said: 'O God, around us and not upon us, O God, upon the hills, the mountains, and the bottoms of valleys.' And all of that is transmitted by tawatur (mass transmission).
Source pages p. 730

Commentary
This passage presents a specific miracle: the Prophet's supplication against the tribe of Mudar. When they harmed and denied him, he prayed for a famine like that of Joseph. His prayer was answered: rain stopped, vegetation died, and livestock perished. Then, when they asked for relief, he prayed again, and rain came so heavily that it destroyed houses. He then redirected the rain to uninhabited areas. The author emphasizes that this is transmitted by tawatur, making it an undeniable proof of the Prophet's prophethood.

Key Terms
دعاء
مضر
تواتر
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The famine was a natural coincidence.
Correction: The author stresses that the event is transmitted by tawatur, establishing it as a certain miracle, not a coincidence.

Checkpoint

A) They became wealthy.
B) They suffered a severe drought.
C) They became Muslims.
D) They were destroyed by an earthquake.

Key Takeaway
This lesson establishes the answered supplication against Mudar as a miracle transmitted by tawatur, confirming the Prophet's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When people harm or reject you because of your faith, do you respond with the same confident du'a as the Prophet? What holds you back from that level of reliance on Allah?
?
The Prophet's du'a was answered immediately. Examine your own habit of supplication: do you truly expect Allah to respond, or do you treat it as a mere ritual? What change must you make today?
?
The tawatur of this event gives you certainty. How will this certainty transform your love for the Prophet and your commitment to his sunna starting this very moment?

The Prophet's Supplication Against Chosroes (Kisra)
The author relates the Prophet's supplication against Chosroes and its fulfillment as a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's supplication against Kisra and its precise fulfillment serve as a miracle validating his prophethood.

Core Idea
A prayer and a prophecy—both fulfilled exactly—confirming the Prophet's truth.

This passage recounts a specific incident where the Persian emperor Kisra tore the Prophet's letter and sent dust. The Prophet responded with a supplication that his kingdom be torn apart, and also foretold that the Muslims would conquer his land. The fulfillment of this prophecy is presented as a clear miracle, demonstrating the truth of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation once. Let the narrative sink in before analyzing.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the supplication and prophecy

The prayer uses the same verb 'maziq' (tear) as Kisra's action.
3
Reflect on the fulfillment as a miracle
Consider that the prophecy was specific and was fulfilled exactly. Ask yourself how this event supports the claim of prophethood.
The author includes this as evidence of prophethood.

Source Text

ومن ذلك دعاؤه على كسرى حين مزق كتابه وبعث إليه بتراب فقال: اللهم مزق ملكه كل ممزق. وقال لأصحابه: مزق كتابي أما إنه ستمزق أمته، وبعث إلي بالتراب أما إنكم ستملكون أرضه. فمزق الله ملكه، وشتت جمعه، وملكهم أرضه.

Source pages p. 730

Commentary
This passage presents another miracle: the Prophet's supplication against Kisra (the Persian emperor). When Kisra tore the Prophet's letter and sent a handful of dust in contempt, the Prophet prayed that his kingdom be utterly torn. He also prophesied that his empire would be divided and that the Muslims would conquer his land. The passage records that this indeed happened: God tore apart his kingdom and the Muslims ruled his territory.

Other Answered Supplications as Miraculous Proofs
Nasafi lists four answered supplications as evidence of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's answered supplications serve as miraculous proofs of his prophethood, and you will be able to identify four specific examples from the text.

Core Idea
Answered prayers are miracles that confirm prophethood.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi continues to present miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) in the form of answered supplications. These are not random stories; they are specific events that demonstrate that only a true prophet could have his prayers answered in such extraordinary ways. We will examine four examples mentioned in the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Note the four specific examples listed.
The passage begins with 'ومن ذلك' and each example starts with 'ومنها'.
2
Identify the four examples
List each answered supplication: against Utbah, for Ibn Abbas, the cave incident, and the sinking horse. Understand the extraordinary nature of each.
These are not ordinary events; they involve divine intervention.
3
Reflect on why these are miracles
Consider how each event could only have occurred through divine response to the Prophet's prayer, thus proving his prophethood.
A false prophet would not have such prayers answered.
4
Consider the author's conclusion
Note the phrase 'وفي ذلك كثرة وفي هذا القدر كفاية' meaning there are many such examples and these few suffice as proof.
This emphasizes the cumulative weight of the evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك دعاؤه على عتبة بن أبي لهب : اللهم سلط عليه كلبًا من كلابك فافترسه الأسد في بعض أسفاره، ومنها دعاؤه لعبد الله بن عباس بالفقه والحكمة فحصل ما دعا، ومنها ما أعمى الله تعالى أبصار الظالمين له حين كان في الغار، ومنها ما ساخ بقوائم فرس من اتبعه في الأرض بدعائه، وفي ذلك كثرة، وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
And among that is his supplication against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab: 'O God, set upon him a dog from Your dogs,' so a lion devoured him on one of his travels. And among them is his supplication for Abdullah ibn Abbas for understanding and wisdom, and what he prayed for was attained. And among them is that God blinded the sight of the oppressors against him when he was in the cave. And among them is that He sank the hooves of the horse of one who followed him into the ground by his supplication. And there is much in that, and in this amount is sufficient.
Source pages p. 731

Commentary
This passage groups several additional miracles of the Prophet's supplications. The first is against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab, who was killed by a lion as prayed. The second is a positive supplication for Abdullah ibn Abbas, who became a great scholar. The third is the miracle of the cave, where the oppressors' sight was blinded. The fourth is a miracle of the earth swallowing a horse's hooves. The author notes that there are many more such examples, indicating that these are sufficient as proof.

Correction: They form a pattern of divine response that collectively proves prophethood, and the author notes there are many such incidents.

Previous Scriptures Foretold the Prophet's Coming
The author introduces the topic of glad tidings in earlier scriptures and begins citing the Torah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how earlier scriptures, particularly the Torah, contained prophecies about the Prophet Muhammad, and why this is evidence for his prophethood.

Core Idea
Earlier scriptures promised the Prophet's coming — a sign of continuity in divine revelation.

This lesson looks at a key argument for the Prophet's truthfulness: that previous scriptures foretold his advent. The author of the Tabṣira begins by citing scholars who collected such prophecies, starting with a passage from the Torah. Though the quote is incomplete here, it points to a broader tradition of recognizing Muhammad in earlier texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the author sets up the topic of glad tidings.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the main claim is clear.
2
Identify the author's claim
What does the author state about previous scriptures? He says scholars have cited many things from them regarding glad tidings of the Prophet's prophethood.
3
Consider the Torah quote
The author begins citing a verse from the Torah: 'God came from Sinai, and shone...' How do you think this relates to the Prophet? In Islamic tradition, this is interpreted as a prophecy.
The full verse is Deuteronomy 33:2 in the Bible.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some claim that Muslims take such verses out of context. Consider how the author assumes a specific interpretive tradition. Is this fair?
This lesson does not resolve the debate but introduces the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما كان راجعًا إلى البشارات الواردة بنبوته فقد أورد العلماء بالكتب المتقدمة أشياء كثيرة، منها ما ذكر في التوراة: جاء الله تعالى من سيناء، وأشرق
As for what pertains to the glad tidings given of his prophethood, scholars have cited many things from the previous scriptures. Among them is what is mentioned in the Torah: 'God came from Sinai, and shone'...
Source pages p. 731

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of previous scriptures (such as the Torah) containing prophecies about the Prophet Muhammad. The author states that scholars have collected many such references, then begins quoting one example from the Torah that speaks of divine manifestation from Sinai, which is interpreted as referring to the Prophet. The passage is incomplete but establishes the claim that prior revelations foretold his coming.

Key Terms
بشارات
الكتب المتقدمة
التوراة
نبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that Muslim scholars take Torah verses out of context to fabricate prophecies about Muhammad.
Correction: The author is citing a long-standing interpretive tradition within Islam that sees the Torah's reference to 'God coming from Sinai' as a metaphor for the revelation of the Torah to Moses, and 'shining from Seir' as the Gospel, and 'appearing from Paran' as the Qur'an. This is not arbitrary but based on a consistent hermeneutical method.

Checkpoint

D) They were silent about him.

Key Takeaway
The mention of glad tidings in previous scriptures serves as evidence that the Prophet's coming was foretold in earlier revelations.

The Prophecy from Sinai, Seir, and Paran
Interpretation of a Torah verse as prophecy for Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'Allah came from Sinai, shone from Seir, and appeared from Paran' is interpreted as a prophecy about Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A single verse foretells three prophets through three locations.

Scholars of earlier scriptures have collected many glad tidings of the Prophet Muhammad. This lesson examines the first prophecy from the Torah, which uses three geographical references to symbolically announce the revelations given to Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. By understanding this interpretation, you will see how the Torah itself pointed to the coming of Islam's final prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how the author unpacks the verse.
The verse is from the Torah, not the Quran.
2
Identify the three locations
The verse mentions Sinai, Seir, and Paran. Identify which prophet is associated with each location and why.
The author explains that Sinai is for Moses, Seir for Jesus, and Paran for Muhammad.
3
Examine the supporting arguments
The author provides a logical question: 'Is there any other place named Paran besides Mecca? And which prophet received a book after Jesus except Muhammad?' Reflect on this reasoning.
This strengthens the identification of Paran with Mecca.

[ الكتب السابقة بشرت بنبوته عليه السلام] وأما ما كان راجعًا إلى البشارات الواردة بنبوته فقد أورد العلماء بالكتب المتقدمة أشياء كثيرة، منها ما ذكر في التوراة: "جاء الله تعالى من سيناء، وأشرق من ساعير، واستعلن من جبال فاران" فكان فيه إخبار عن إنزال التوراة على موسى عليه السلام بطور سيناء، وإنزاله الإنجيل على عيسى عليه السلام بساعير فإنه كان يسكن من ساعير بقرية تدعى ناصرة، وباسمها سمى من اتبعه نصاری وإنزاله القرآن على محمد والله بجبال فاران وهي جبال مكة، إذ فاران هي مكة، يقر بذلك أهل الكتاب، فإن فى التوراة أن إبراهيم عليه السلام أسكن هاجر - رضي الله عنها - وإسماعيل عليه السلام فاران ويقال لهم : ما الموضع الذي استعلن الله منه : فلا ذلك واسمه فاران سوى مكة ؟ ومن النبي الذي أنزل عليه الكتاب بعد عیسی سوی محمد؟ ومنها ما ذكر في التوراة لموسى في السفر الخامس: "إني أقيم لبني إسرائيل نبيًا من إخوتهم مثلك أجعل كلامي على فمه" فأخوة بني إسرائيل بنو إسماعيل، كما أن أخوة بكر هم تغلب، وأخوة تغلب، وأخوة عيسى هم ذبيان وأخوة الأوس هم الخزرج، ومثل موسى من الأنبياء ليس إلا نبي الله محمد عليه السلام، لما أنه صاحب شريعة مستأنفة فيها بين مصالح الدارين، وليس لأحد سواه من الأنبياء بعد موسى يصح صرفهم هذا الكلام إلى بعض أنبياء بني إسرائيل، لما ليس أحد منهم مثل موسى عليه السلام، وكذا هم من أنفسهم لا من إخوتهم ، ألا ترى أن من قال لآخر: ائتني برجل من أخوة بني بكر بن وائل لكان يجب عليه أن يأتيه برجل من بني تغلب لا برجل من بني بكر، ومنها ما ذكر في الزبور "تقلد أيها الجبار السيف فإن ناموسك وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك وسهامك مسنونة والأمم يخرون تحتك" وليس المتقلد بالسيف من الأنبياء إلا نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وهو الذي خرت الأمم تحته وقرنت شرائعه بالهيبة ومنها ما قال في الزبور . قال :داود: "اللهم ابعث جاعل السنة حتى يعلم الناس أنه بشر وهذا إخبار عن المسيح وعن محمد عليهما السلام يريد ابعث محمدًا حتى يعلم الناس أن عيسى بشر. فعلم داود أن قوما
[Previous scriptures gave glad tidings of his prophethood] As for what relates to the glad tidings of his prophethood, scholars have mentioned many things from the previous scriptures. Among them is what is mentioned in the Torah: 'Allah came from Sinai, shone forth from Seir, and appeared from the mountains of Paran.' In this is information about the revelation of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai; the revelation of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he lived in a village called Nazareth from Seir, and by its name his followers are called Christians; and the revelation of the Quran to Muhammad, peace be upon him, at the mountains of Paran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Paran is Mecca. This is affirmed by the People of the Book, for in the Torah, Abraham, peace be upon him, settled Hagar, may Allah be pleased with her, and Ishmael, peace be upon him, in Paran. And it is said to them: What place did Allah appear from? Is there any other place named Paran besides Mecca? And which prophet was revealed a book after Jesus except Muhammad? Among them is what is mentioned in the Torah to Moses in the fifth book: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brethren like you, and I will put My words in his mouth.' The brethren of the Children of Israel are the Children of Ishmael, just as the brethren of Bakr are Taghlib, and the brethren of Taghlib, and the brethren of Jesus are Dhibyan, and the brethren of Aws are Khazraj. And the only prophet like Moses is the Prophet of Allah, Muhammad, peace be upon him, because he is the possessor of a new Law that combines the interests of both worlds. And no other prophet after Moses can be the referent of this speech among the prophets of the Children of Israel, because none of them is like Moses, peace be upon him. Moreover, they are from themselves, not from their brethren. Do you not see that if someone says to another, 'Bring me a man from the brethren of Bakr ibn Wa'il,' he must bring a man from Taghlib, not a man from Bakr? Among them is what is mentioned in the Zabur: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the majesty of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you.' And the only prophet who girds the sword among the prophets is our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and it is he under whom the nations fell and his laws were accompanied by majesty. Among them is what is said in the Zabur. David said: 'O Allah, send the maker of the Sunnah until the people know that he is a human.' And this is information about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both. He intends: Send Muhammad so that the people know that Jesus is a human. Thus David knew that a people...
Source pages p. 731

Commentary
This passage presents prophecies from previous scriptures about the coming of Prophet Muhammad. It begins by stating that scholars have collected many glad tidings from earlier books. The first prophecy is from the Torah: 'Allah came from Sinai, shone from Seir, and appeared from Paran.' The author explains that this refers to the revelations given to Moses (Sinai), Jesus (Seir, i.e., Nazareth), and Muhammad (Paran, i.e., Mecca). He argues that the People of the Book acknowledge Paran as Mecca. The second prophecy is from Deuteronomy: 'I will raise up a prophet from among their brethren like you.' The author interprets 'their brethren' as the Ishmaelites, not the Israelites themselves, using analogies from Arab tribal relationships. He argues that the only prophet like Moses after him is Muhammad, who brought a comprehensive law. The third prophecy is from the Psalms (Zabur): 'Gird your sword, O mighty one...' which describes a prophet who wields the sword and subdues nations, identified as Muhammad. The fourth prophecy, also from the Zabur, is a supplication of David asking Allah to send the 'maker of the Sunnah' to clarify that Jesus is human. This passage is incomplete, ending abruptly during the explanation of David's knowledge.

Key Terms
سيناء
ساعير
فاران
توراة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, which prophet is associated with the name 'Seir'?
A) Moses
B) Jesus
C) Muhammad
D) Abraham

Key Takeaway
The Torah verse uses three locations to prophetically announce the revelations given to Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Torah verse indeed prophesies Muhammad, how does that shape your view of the consistency of divine revelation across different prophets?
?
Do you personally rely on such biblical prophecies as part of your conviction in Islam, or do you find other proofs stronger? What does this verse do for your faith?
?
When you consider that many people reject this interpretation, how do you maintain certainty in the truth of Muhammad's prophethood? What would you say to someone who dismisses this as forced interpretation?

Prophethood
intermediate
5 min
The Prophecy of a Prophet Like Moses
Interpretation of a Deuteronomy prophecy about a prophet like Moses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the prophecy in Deuteronomy about a prophet from the brethren of Israel refers specifically to Muhammad, not any Israelite prophet.

Core Idea
The 'brethren' of Israel are the Ishmaelites, not the Israelites themselves.

The Torah contains a clear prophecy: 'I will raise up a prophet from among their brethren like you.' This lesson unpacks the author's argument that 'brethren' means the Ishmaelites, using tribal analogies from Arab culture. He then demonstrates that the only prophet after Moses who fits the description is Muhammad, who brought a new comprehensive law.

Guided Path
1
Read the Torah quotation
Read the verse from Deuteronomy carefully: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brethren like you.'
The verse is from the fifth book of Moses.
2
Understand the tribal analogy
The author gives examples: the brethren of Bakr are Taghlib, not Bakr themselves. Similarly, the brethren of Israel are Ishmaelites, not Israelites.
This clarifies that 'their brethren' excludes the Children of Israel themselves.
3
Identify the prophet like Moses
The author argues that no other prophet after Moses is like him except Muhammad, who brought a new law covering both this world and the Hereafter.
Moses and Muhammad both brought comprehensive laws.
