Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the prophecy refers to an Israelite prophet like Joshua or Jeremiah.
Correction: The author shows that 'brethren' excludes Israelites, and only Muhammad matches 'like Moses' in bringing a new law.

?

?

Prophethood

Prophecies from the Zabur
Two Zabur prophecies: one about a sword-wielding prophet, one about the maker of the Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two passages from the Zabur (Psalms) prophesy about Prophet Muhammad and clarify the humanity of Jesus.

Core Idea
The Zabur describes a prophet who wields the sword and introduces a law with majesty.

The Zabur (Psalms) also contains prophecies about the coming of Muhammad. This lesson covers two such prophecies. The first describes a prophet who girds his sword and subdues nations, which the author identifies as Muhammad. The second is a supplication of David asking Allah to send the 'maker of the Sunnah' so that people know Jesus is human. Though the passage is incomplete, the available text shows how the Psalms foretold key aspects of Muhammad's mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the first Zabur prophecy
Read the verse about girding the sword and the nations falling under him. Notice the author's commentary.
The sword is a symbol of military leadership and law enforcement.
2
Identify the prophet with the sword
The author states that only Muhammad among prophets girded the sword, referring to his military campaigns.
This distinguishes Muhammad from previous prophets who did not engage in armed conflict.
3
Read the incomplete second prophecy
Read David's supplication about the 'maker of the Sunnah' and how it relates to Jesus' humanity.
The passage is cut off, but the intention is to show that Muhammad would clarify Jesus' true nature.

The third prophecy is from the Psalms (Zabur): 'Gird your sword, O mighty one...' which describes a prophet who wields the sword and subdues nations, identified as Muhammad. The fourth prophecy, also from the Zabur, is a supplication of David asking Allah to send the 'maker of the Sunnah' to clarify that Jesus is human. This passage is incomplete, ending abruptly during the explanation of David's knowledge.

سيف

ناموس
سنّة

Key Takeaway
The Zabur contains prophecies that Muhammad would wield a sword and establish a majestic law, and that he would clarify Jesus' humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Zabur foretold a prophet with a sword and a majestic law. Do you fully accept Muhammad as that prophet, or do you hesitate when you think of his military campaigns? How does this prophecy reshape your understanding of his mission?
?
David prayed for a 'maker of the Sunnah' to clarify that Jesus is human. Do you truly believe that Jesus was a human prophet, or does any remnant of doubt linger? How will you actively reinforce this belief in your heart today?
?
These prophecies were preserved in the Psalms. If God foretold Muhammad's coming in ancient scriptures, what does that demand of you regarding your faith in the continuity of revelation? Will you study the Zabur prophecies more deeply to strengthen your conviction?

Scriptural Proofs for Muhammad's Prophethood
Al-Nasafi cites specific scriptural proofs from Torah, Psalms, and Gospel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses scriptural references from the Torah, Psalms, and Gospel to argue that Muhammad was foretold in previous scriptures.

Core Idea
Previous scriptures geographically and textually point to Muhammad.

In this passage, Al-Nasafi presents several proofs from the Torah, Psalms, and Gospel that indicate the coming of Muhammad. He begins with a geographical parallel between the revelations and then cites specific verses. This lesson covers the scriptural evidence he brings forward before turning to a rational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the geographical parallel
Notice how the locations of revelation (Sinai, Seir, Faran) mirror each other, establishing a pattern. This sets the stage for scriptural proofs.
Faran is identified as Mecca, tying the Qur'an's revelation to earlier books.
2
Examine the Torah prophecy
Al-Nasafi cites Deuteronomy 18:18 about a prophet like Moses from the brothers of Israel. Understand the reasoning that 'brothers' means Ishmaelites (Arabs), not Israelites themselves.
He argues that only Muhammad fits this description as a law-giver like Moses.
3
Consider the Psalms and Gospel references
Identify the verses from Psalms about the sword and the one who establishes the Sunnah, and the Gospel's mention of the Paraclete. Note how they are applied to Muhammad.
The Paraclete is interpreted as 'Spirit of Truth' who will teach all things.
4
Reflect on the People of the Book's distortion
Al-Nasafi acknowledges that the People of the Book do not deny these texts exist but distort their interpretation. This sets up his rational argument in the next lesson.
He mentions that kalam scholars have refuted these distortions.

من ساعير، واستعلن من جبال فاران فكان فيه إخبار عن إنزال التوراة على موسى عليه السلام بطور سيناء، وإنزاله الإنجيل على عيسى عليه السلام بساعير فإنه كان يسكن من ساعير بقرية تدعى ناصرة، وباسمها سمى من اتبعه نصاری وإنزاله القرآن على محمد والله بجبال فاران وهي جبال مكة، إذ فاران هي مكة، يقر بذلك أهل الكتاب، فإن فى التوراة أن إبراهيم عليه السلام أسكن هاجر - رضي الله عنها - وإسماعيل عليه السلام فاران ويقال لهم : ما الموضع الذي استعلن الله منه : فلا ذلك واسمه فاران سوى مكة ؟ ومن النبي الذي أنزل عليه الكتاب بعد عیسی سوی محمد؟ ومنها ما ذكر في التوراة لموسى في السفر الخامس: "إني أقيم لبني إسرائيل نبيًا من إخوتهم مثلك أجعل كلامي على فمه فأخوة بني إسرائيل بنو إسماعيل، كما أن أخوة بكر هم تغلب، وأخوة تغلب، وأخوة عيسى هم ذبيان وأخوة الأوس هم الخزرج، ومثل موسى من الأنبياء ليس إلا نبي الله محمد عليه السلام، لما أنه صاحب شريعة مستأنفة فيها بين مصالح الدارين، وليس لأحد سواه من الأنبياء بعد موسى يصح صرفهم هذا الكلام إلى بعض أنبياء بني إسرائيل، لما ليس أحد منهم مثل موسى عليه السلام، وكذا هم من أنفسهم لا من إخوتهم ، ألا ترى أن من قال لآخر: ائتني برجل من أخوة بني بكر بن وائل لكان يجب عليه أن يأتيه برجل من بني تغلب لا برجل من بني بكر، ومنها ما ذكر في الزبور "تقلد أيها الجبار السيف فإن ناموسك وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك وسهامك مسنونة والأمم يخرون تحتك" وليس المتقلد للسيف من الأنبياء إلا نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وهو الذي خرت الأمم تحته وقرنت شرائعه بالهيبة ومنها ما قال في الزبور . قال داود: "اللهم ابعث جاعل السنة حتى يعلم الناس أنه بشر" وهذا إخبار عن المسيح وعن محمد عليهما السلام يريد ابعث محمدًا حتى يعلم الناس أن عيسى بشر. فعلم داود أن قوما سيدعون للمسيح ما ادعوا . ومنها ألفاظ كثيرة في الإنجيل باسم فارقليط من ذلك أن الفارقليط روح الحق الذي يرسله أي باسمي هو يعلمك كل شيء. ذكر العلماء بكتبهم هذه الألفاظ وأشياء كثيرة من كتب الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام فيها ذكره وذكر أصحابه وذكر مكة والكعبة والحرم والحجر وغير ذلك لا ينكر أهل الكتابين ثبوت ذلك غير أنهم يحرفون الكلم من مواضعه ويصرفون ذلك كله بتأويلات مستكرهة فاسدة إلى غير ما هو المراد، وقد ذكر ذلك أئمة أهل الكلام، وأبطلوا تأويلاتهم الفاسدة، وأعرضت عن ذكر ذلك مخافة الإطالة واكتفيت من ذلك كله بمعقول لا اعتراض للخصوم عليه ولا انفصال لهم عنه وهو أن محمدًا ادعى أنه مذكور في كتبهم وأنه مبشر به على لسان المسيح على ما ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله : ( الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ وَالإِنجِيلِ ) ، وقال تعالى خبرًا عن عيسى عليه السلام: إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُم مُّصَدِّقًا لِّمَا بَيْنَ يَدَيَّ مِنَ التَّوْرَاةِ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولٍ يَأْتِي مِن بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ (١) وقال تعالى: ﴿ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تَكْفُرُونَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنتُمْ تَشْهَدُونَ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَبِ لِمَ تَلْبِسُونَ الْحَقَّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَأَنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ )) . وقال : الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ ) وفي آيات كثيرة يطول تعدادها وقد كان يدعوهم إلى اتباعه وتصديقه، وقد أقام على صحة دعواه من الدلالات الكافية التي قطعت أعذار الجاحدين، فكيف كان يحتج عليهم بباطل ويحيل ذلك إلى ما عندهم وفي أيديهم ويقول علامة ثبوتي ودليل صدقي أنكم تجدونني مكتوبًا وهو يعلم أنهم لا يجدونه، ويعلم أن ذلك مما يزيدهم نفارًا وعما يدعوهم إليه بعدًا، وقد كان غنيًا عن ذلك بما أقام من الدلالات، أيفعل ذلك
From Seir, and He manifested from the mountains of Faran, for in it there is news of the revelation of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai, and the revelation of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he used to dwell in Seir in a village called Nazareth, and by its name those who followed him were called Christians, and the revelation of the Qur'an to Muhammad, peace be upon him, at the mountains of Faran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Faran is Mecca—the People of the Book affirm that. For in the Torah, Abraham, peace be upon him, settled Hagar—may God be pleased with her—and Ishmael, peace be upon him, in Faran. And it is said to them: What is the place from which God manifested? Is it not that whose name is Faran, other than Mecca? And who is the prophet upon whom the Book was revealed after Jesus, other than Muhammad? And among it is what is mentioned in the Torah to Moses in the fifth book: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers like you; I will put My words in his mouth.' So the brothers of the Children of Israel are the Children of Ishmael, just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, the brothers of Taghlib, the brothers of Jesus are Dhubyan, and the brothers of Aws are Khazraj. And a prophet like Moses among the prophets is none other than the Prophet of God, Muhammad, peace be upon him, because he is the possessor of a new law comprising the interests of both abodes. And there is no one else among the prophets after Moses to whom it is correct to apply this speech to any prophet of the Children of Israel, because not one of them is like Moses, peace be upon him. Moreover, they are from among themselves, not from their brothers. Do you not see that if someone says to another, 'Bring me a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr ibn Wa'il,' he would have to bring him a man from Banu Taghlib, not from Banu Bakr? And among it is what is mentioned in the Psalms: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and nations fall beneath you.' And the one who girded the sword among the prophets is none other than our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and it is he under whom nations fell and his laws were accompanied by awe. And among it is what David said in the Psalms: 'O God, send the one who establishes the Sunnah so that people may know that he is human.' This is news about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both—meaning, send Muhammad so that people may know that Jesus is human. Thus David knew that a people would claim for the Christ what they claimed. And among it are many expressions in the Gospel under the name 'Paraclete,' such as that the Paraclete is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends in My name; He will teach you everything. The scholars mentioned these expressions in their books, and many things from the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, containing mention of him, mention of his companions, mention of Mecca, the Ka'ba, the Sanctuary, the Stone, and other things. The two Peoples of the Book do not deny the existence of that, but they distort the words from their places and interpret all of that with repugnant false interpretations to other than what is intended. The imams of the people of kalam have mentioned that and invalidated their false interpretations. I have refrained from mentioning that for fear of prolongation, and I have sufficed from all that with a rational argument that the opponents cannot object to nor escape from: namely, that Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their books and that he was given glad tidings by the tongue of Christ, according to what God Almighty mentioned in His Book by His saying: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' (7:157). And God Almighty said, informing about Jesus, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, I am the messenger of God to you, confirming what came before me of the Torah and giving glad tidings of a messenger to come after me whose name is Ahmad' (61:6). And God Almighty said: 'O People of the Scripture, why do you disbelieve in the verses of God while you witness? O People of the Scripture, why do you mix the truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know?' (3:70-71). And He said: 'Those to whom We gave the Scripture recognize him as they recognize their own sons' (2:146). And there are many verses whose enumeration would be lengthy. And he used to call them to follow and believe him, and he established for the soundness of his claim sufficient proofs that cut off the excuses of the deniers. So how could he argue against them with falsehood and refer that to what they have in their hands, saying, 'The sign of my establishment and the proof of my truthfulness is that you find me written [in your books]'—while he knows that they do not find it, and he knows that that would increase their aversion and distance from what he calls them to? And he was independent of that by the proofs he established. Would he do that?
Source pages p. 732

Commentary
This passage presents a cumulative argument for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) from previous scriptures, followed by a rational argument that refutes the need for detailed scriptural citation.

The author begins by noting a geographical parallel: the Torah was revealed on Mount Sinai, the Gospel in the region of Seir (associated with Jesus in Nazareth), and the Qur'an at the mountains of Faran (Mecca). This parallel is attested by the People of the Book themselves, who acknowledge that Abraham settled Hagar and Ishmael in Faran (Mecca). The author then poses rhetorical questions: Where else could God have manifested but Faran (Mecca)? And which prophet after Jesus received a scripture other than Muhammad?

Next, three specific scriptural testimonies are cited:
1. From the Torah (Deuteronomy 18:18): God promises to raise up a prophet like Moses from among the brothers of the Children of Israel. The author explains that the "brothers" of Israel are the Ishmaelites (Arabs), just as the brothers of a specific Arab tribe are another tribe. The only prophet from the Ishmaelites who brought a new law (shari'a) like Moses is Muhammad. He refutes any application to prophets from among the Children of Israel themselves, as they are not "brothers" but from within.
2. From the Psalms: a verse about a mighty one girding a sword, with laws accompanied by awe and nations falling under him. The author identifies this as unique to Muhammad, who wielded the sword in jihad and whose law was established with awe among nations.
3. Another Psalm verse: David prays for the one who establishes the Sunnah (Muhammad) so that people may know that Jesus is human. This shows that David foresaw that some would exaggerate about Jesus (claiming divinity) and that Muhammad would reveal the truth.
4. From the Gospel: mention of the Paraclete (Spirit of Truth) who would teach everything—interpreted by scholars as referring to Muhammad.

The author notes that the People of the Book do not deny the existence of these texts in their scriptures, but they distort and misinterpret them. The imams of kalam have refuted these distortions.

Then the author makes a key methodological point: he refrains from enumerating all such citations for fear of prolixity, and instead presents a simple rational argument (ma'qul) that the opponents cannot escape: Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their scriptures, as affirmed by multiple Qur'anic verses (7:157, 61:6, 3:70-71, 2:146). He called them to follow him and provided clear proofs (miracles, etc.) that sufficed to establish his truthfulness. If his claim to be found in their scriptures were false, and he knew they would not find it, that would only increase their aversion—and he would have been foolish to rely on a false claim when he already had overwhelming proofs. Therefore, the fact that he confidently made this claim, coupled with his other proofs, demonstrates that he was indeed foretold in their books. This rational argument shifts the burden back to the opponents.

Key Terms

ساعير
جبال فاران
فارقليط
الزبور
التوراة
الإنجيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scriptural proofs are the only way to prove Muhammad's prophethood.
Correction: Al-Nasafi later introduces a rational argument that doesn't rely on detailed citation, showing that he values multiple types of proof.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, to whom does the Torah prophecy in Deuteronomy 18:18 refer?
A) A prophet from the Children of Israel
B) A prophet from the brothers of the Children of Israel, i.e., Ishmaelites
C) Jesus Christ
D) David

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi uses scriptural references to show that Muhammad is foretold, but he acknowledges that opponents twist them, leading to a rational argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The People of the Book had clear prophecies about Muhammad in their scriptures, yet they distorted them. Is there any truth about your own faith that you have been avoiding or twisting because accepting it would require you to change your lifestyle? What will you do today to confront that truth honestly?
?
The geographical path of revelation—from Sinai to Seir to Faran—shows that Allah's plan unfolds deliberately across time and place. Do you see your own life as part of that grand divine narrative, or do you live as if your days are random and without purpose? How can you remind yourself daily that your existence is a deliberate station on the Prophet's path?
?
David prayed for the one who would establish the Sunnah so that people would know that Jesus is human. This prophecy combats both exaggeration and neglect of the prophets. In your heart, do you lean toward exaggeration (e.g., attributing divine qualities to the Prophet ﷺ) or neglect (e.g., not following his sunnah sincerely)? What is one concrete, non-negotiable sunnah you will commit to practicing this week to align with the middle path?

Prophethood
intermediate

The Rational Argument from Scriptural Claim
Al-Nasafi presents a rational argument that Muhammad's prophethood is confirmed by his claim being backed by miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's rational argument that Muhammad's claim to be foretold in scriptures must be true because of his other overwhelming proofs.

Core Idea
Muhammad's confident claim plus clear proofs proves his foretelling.

After presenting scriptural proofs, Al-Nasafi shifts to a rational argument that does not require detailed citation. He argues that Muhammad had established his prophethood with clear miracles, so his claim to be found in previous books cannot be false; otherwise it would be counterproductive. This lesson unpacks the logic of this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transition
Al-Nasafi says he refrains from more citations for fear of prolixity and suffices with a rational argument. Notice the shift from scriptural to rational approach.
This shows his methodological awareness.
2
Understand the rational argument
The argument: Muhammad claimed to be foretold in scriptures. He had clear proofs (miracles) for his prophethood. If his claim were false, it would repel people, contradicting his wisdom. Therefore, his claim must be true.
This is a transcendental argument, not a simple scriptural one.
3
See the backing with Qur'anic verses
Al-Nasafi cites several Qur'an verses that assert Muhammad is foretold in previous books (e.g., 7:157, 61:6, 3:70-71, 2:146) to show that the Qur'an itself affirms this.
The verses are the source of the claim, not the Torah/Gospel directly.
4
Reflect on the strength of the argument
This argument shifts the burden to the opponents: they cannot deny that Muhammad made this claim and had clear proofs. The assumption that he was truthful and wise leads to the conclusion that his claim is correct.
It avoids having to settle textual disputes.

والحرم والحجر وغير ذلك لا ينكر أهل الكتابين ثبوت ذلك غير أنهم يحرفون الكلم من مواضعه ويصرفون ذلك كله بتأويلات مستكرهة فاسدة إلى غير ما هو المراد، وقد ذكر ذلك أئمة أهل الكلام، وأبطلوا تأويلاتهم الفاسدة، وأعرضت عن ذكر ذلك مخافة الإطالة واكتفيت من ذلك كله بمعقول لا اعتراض للخصوم عليه ولا انفصال لهم عنه وهو أن محمدًا ادعى أنه مذكور في كتبهم وأنه مبشر به على لسان المسيح على ما ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله : ( الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ وَالإِنجِيلِ ) ، وقال تعالى خبرًا عن عيسى عليه السلام: إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُم مُّصَدِّقًا لِّمَا بَيْنَ يَدَيَّ مِنَ التَّوْرَاةِ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولٍ يَأْتِي مِن بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ (١) وقال تعالى: ﴿ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تَكْفُرُونَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنتُمْ تَشْهَدُونَ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَبِ لِمَ تَلْبِسُونَ الْحَقَّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَأَنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ )) . وقال : الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ ) وفي آيات كثيرة يطول تعدادها وقد كان يدعوهم إلى اتباعه وتصديقه، وقد أقام على صحة دعواه من الدلالات الكافية التي قطعت أعذار الجاحدين، فكيف كان يحتج عليهم بباطل ويحيل ذلك إلى ما عندهم وفي أيديهم ويقول علامة ثبوتي ودليل صدقي أنكم تجدونني مكتوبًا وهو يعلم أنهم لا يجدونه، ويعلم أن ذلك مما يزيدهم نفارًا وعما يدعوهم إليه بعدًا، وقد كان غنيًا عن ذلك بما أقام من الدلالات، أيفعل ذلك
From Seir, and He manifested from the mountains of Faran, for in it there is news of the revelation of the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, at Mount Sinai, and the revelation of the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, at Seir, for he used to dwell in Seir in a village called Nazareth, and by its name those who followed him were called Christians, and the revelation of the Qur'an to Muhammad, peace be upon him, at the mountains of Faran, which are the mountains of Mecca, for Faran is Mecca—the People of the Book affirm that. For in the Torah, Abraham, peace be upon him, settled Hagar—may God be pleased with her—and Ishmael, peace be upon him, in Faran. And it is said to them: What is the place from which God manifested? Is it not that whose name is Faran, other than Mecca? And who is the prophet upon whom the Book was revealed after Jesus, other than Muhammad? And among it is what is mentioned in the Torah to Moses in the fifth book: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brothers like you; I will put My words in his mouth.' So the brothers of the Children of Israel are the Children of Ishmael, just as the brothers of Bakr are Taghlib, the brothers of Taghlib, the brothers of Jesus are Dhubyan, and the brothers of Aws are Khazraj. And a prophet like Moses among the prophets is none other than the Prophet of God, Muhammad, peace be upon him, because he is the possessor of a new law comprising the interests of both abodes. And there is no one else among the prophets after Moses to whom it is correct to apply this speech to any prophet of the Children of Israel, because not one of them is like Moses, peace be upon him. Moreover, they are from among themselves, not from their brothers. Do you not see that if someone says to another, 'Bring me a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr ibn Wa'il,' he would have to bring him a man from Banu Taghlib, not from Banu Bakr? And among it is what is mentioned in the Psalms: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and nations fall beneath you.' And the one who girded the sword among the prophets is none other than our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and it is he under whom nations fell and his laws were accompanied by awe. And among it is what David said in the Psalms: 'O God, send the one who establishes the Sunnah so that people may know that he is human.' This is news about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both—meaning, send Muhammad so that people may know that Jesus is human. Thus David knew that a people would claim for the Christ what they claimed. And among it are many expressions in the Gospel under the name 'Paraclete,' such as that the Paraclete is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends in My name; He will teach you everything. The scholars mentioned these expressions in their books, and many things from the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, containing mention of him, mention of his companions, mention of Mecca, the Ka'ba, the Sanctuary, the Stone, and other things. The two Peoples of the Book do not deny the existence of that, but they distort the words from their places and interpret all of that with repugnant false interpretations to other than what is intended. The imams of the people of kalam have mentioned that and invalidated their false interpretations. I have refrained from mentioning that for fear of prolongation, and I have sufficed from all that with a rational argument that the opponents cannot object to nor escape from: namely, that Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their books and that he was given glad tidings by the tongue of Christ, according to what God Almighty mentioned in His Book by His saying: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' (7:157). And God Almighty said, informing about Jesus, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, I am the messenger of God to you, confirming what came before me of the Torah and giving glad tidings of a messenger to come after me whose name is Ahmad' (61:6). And God Almighty said: 'O People of the Scripture, why do you disbelieve in the verses of God while you witness? O People of the Scripture, why do you mix the truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know?' (3:70-71). And He said: 'Those to whom We gave the Scripture recognize him as they recognize their own sons' (2:146). And there are many verses whose enumeration would be lengthy. And he used to call them to follow and believe him, and he established for the soundness of his claim sufficient proofs that cut off the excuses of the deniers. So how could he argue against them with falsehood and refer that to what they have in their hands, saying, 'The sign of my establishment and the proof of my truthfulness is that you find me written [in your books]'—while he knows that they do not find it, and he knows that that would increase their aversion and distance from what he calls them to? And he was independent of that by the proofs he established. Would he do that?
Source pages p. 732

Commentary
This passage presents a cumulative argument for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) from previous scriptures, followed by a rational argument that refutes the need for detailed scriptural citation.

The author begins by noting a geographical parallel: the Torah was revealed on Mount Sinai, the Gospel in the region of Seir (associated with Jesus in Nazareth), and the Qur'an at the mountains of Faran (Mecca). This parallel is attested by the People of the Book themselves, who acknowledge that Abraham settled Hagar and Ishmael in Faran (Mecca). The author then poses rhetorical questions: Where else could God have manifested but Faran (Mecca)? And which prophet after Jesus received a scripture other than Muhammad?

Next, three specific scriptural testimonies are cited:
1. From the Torah (Deuteronomy 18:18): God promises to raise up a prophet like Moses from among the brothers of the Children of Israel. The author explains that the "brothers" of Israel are the Ishmaelites (Arabs), just as the brothers of a specific Arab tribe are another tribe. The only prophet from the Ishmaelites who brought a new law (shari'a) like Moses is Muhammad. He refutes any application to prophets from among the Children of Israel themselves, as they are not "brothers" but from within.
2. From the Psalms: a verse about a mighty one girding a sword, with laws accompanied by awe and nations falling under him. The author identifies this as unique to Muhammad, who wielded the sword in jihad and whose law was established with awe among nations.
3. Another Psalm verse: David prays for the one who establishes the Sunnah (Muhammad) so that people may know that Jesus is human. This shows that David foresaw that some would exaggerate about Jesus (claiming divinity) and that Muhammad would reveal the truth.
4. From the Gospel: mention of the Paraclete (Spirit of Truth) who would teach everything—interpreted by scholars as referring to Muhammad.

The author notes that the People of the Book do not deny the existence of these texts in their scriptures, but they distort and misinterpret them. The imams of kalam have refuted these distortions.

Then the author makes a key methodological point: he refrains from enumerating all such citations for fear of prolixity, and instead presents a simple rational argument (ma'qul) that the opponents cannot escape: Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their scriptures, as affirmed by multiple Qur'anic verses (7:157, 61:6, 3:70-71, 2:146). He called them to follow him and provided clear proofs (miracles, etc.) that sufficed to establish his truthfulness. If his claim to be found in their scriptures were false, and he knew they would not find it, that would only increase their aversion—and he would have been foolish to rely on a false claim when he already had overwhelming proofs. Therefore, the fact that he confidently made this claim, coupled with his other proofs, demonstrates that he was indeed foretold in their books. This rational argument shifts the burden back to the opponents.

Key Terms
معقول
المسيح
أحمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Nasafi relies purely on reason and abandons scripture.
Correction: He actually uses a rational argument that is based on the fact of Muhammad's claim, which is mentioned in the Qur'an, so scripture is still foundational.

Checkpoint
What is the core of Al-Nasafi's rational argument?
A) He provides many scriptural citations to prove the claim.
B) He argues that Muhammad's claim to be foretold, combined with his clear proofs, makes it impossible that he was lying.
C) He says the People of the Book agree with Muhammad.
D) He relies on consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi's rational argument provides a powerful defense that shifts the burden to opponents without requiring detailed scriptural debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that just as truthfulness is required for a prophet, consistency demands that we examine our own beliefs. Are there areas in your life where you claim to follow the Prophet but your actions contradict his teachings? What specific step will you take today to align your actions with your claims?
?
The rational argument relies on the impossibility of a wise person making a self-defeating claim. Consider your own testimony about Islam: do you truly believe that the Prophet's proofs are sufficient, or do you harbor doubts that you have not confronted? What is one doubt you need to face and resolve through study or sincere supplication?
?
If someone challenged you with the same argument Al-Nasafi presents, could you explain it convincingly? Reflect on your own understanding of the proofs of prophethood. What will you do this week to deepen your certainty in the truth of Muhammad's message?

Prophethood

Proof of Prophethood from Scripture and Reason
Nasafi presents the proof from scripture mentions and the rational argument against false claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi combines scriptural mentions and rational argument to prove the Prophet's mention in earlier scriptures.

Core Idea
The Prophet's claim of scriptural foretelling is proven by the impossibility of a wise person making a false claim easily refuted.

Nasafi presents a dual proof for prophethood: the existence of the Prophet's mention in earlier scriptures and a rational argument that such a claim could not be false given the Prophet's wisdom and the testimony of knowledgeable converts. In this passage, he outlines both the scriptural basis and the logical reasoning that makes the case compelling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scriptural evidence
Read the passage and note the specific references to the Paraclete and the verses from the Quran that claim the Prophet is mentioned in the Torah and Gospel.
Nasafi acknowledges that opponents distort these texts but insists the references are clear.
2
Understand the rational argument
Focus on the rhetorical question: 'Would a madman do that?' This is the core of the rational proof. The Prophet's wisdom and the conversion of learned rabbis make his claim undeniable.
The argument hinges on the impossibility of a wise person persisting in a false claim that could be easily disproved by opponents.
3
Review additional evidence
Notice Nasafi also cites mentions in Persian and Yemeni traditions. This shows the breadth of attestation across cultures.
This reinforces the proof by showing that the Prophet's coming was expected by multiple nations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سيدعون للمسيح ما ادعوا . ومنها ألفاظ كثيرة في الإنجيل باسم فارقليط من ذلك أن الفارقليط روح الحق الذي يرسله أي باسمي هو يعلمك كل شيء. ذكر العلماء بكتبهم هذه الألفاظ وأشياء كثيرة من كتب الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام فيها ذكره وذكر أصحابه وذكر مكة والكعبة والحرم والحجر وغير ذلك لا ينكر أهل الكتابين ثبوت ذلك غير أنهم يحرفون الكلم من مواضعه ويصرفون ذلك كله بتأويلات مستكرهة فاسدة إلى غير ما هو المراد، وقد ذكر ذلك أئمة أهل الكلام، وأبطلوا تأويلاتهم الفاسدة، وأعرضت عن ذكر ذلك مخافة الإطالة واكتفيت من ذلك كله بمعقول لا اعتراض للخصوم عليه ولا انفصال لهم عنه وهو أن محمدًا ادعى أنه مذكور في كتبهم وأنه مبشر به على لسان المسيح على ما ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله : ( الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُتِيَ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَنة والإنجيل ) ، وقال تعالى خبرًا عن عيسى عليه السلام: إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُم مُّصَدِّقَالِمَا بيْنَ يَدَيَّ مِنَ التَّوْرَيَةِ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولٍ يَأْتِي مِنْ بَعْدِى اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ ) وقال تعالى: ﴿ يَتَأَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تكفُرُونَ بِشَايَتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنتُمْ تَشْهَدُونَ يَتَأَهْلَ الْكِتَبِ لِمَ تَلْبِسُونَ الْحَقِّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقِّ وَأَنتُم تعلَمُونَ )) . وقال : الَّذِينَ ءَاتَيْنَهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ ) وفي آيات كثيرة يطول تعدادها وقد كان يدعوهم إلى اتباعه وتصديقه، وقد أقام على صحة دعواه من الدلالات الكافية التي قطعت أعذار الجاحدين، فكيف كان يحتج عليهم بباطل ويحيل ذلك إلى ما عندهم وفي أيديهم ويقول علامة ثبوتي ودليل صدقي أنكم تجدونني مكتوبًا وهو يعلم أنهم لا يجدونه، ويعلم أن ذلك مما يزيدهم نفارًا وعما يدعوهم إليه بعدًا، وقد كان غنيًا عن ذلك بما أقام من الدلالات، أيفعل ذلك مجنون؟ فضلاً عمن طبقت حكمته الأرض، وفاق على زعم الخصوم جميع أهل الأرض دهاء وذكاء وأبذ على كافة الفصحاء في البلاغة والفصاحة، ولم أسلم والحال كما زعموا من كذبه في دعواه وجود ذكره والبشارة به في الكتب المتقدمة - من أسلم من علمائهم وأحبارهم كعبد الله بن سلام وتميم الداري وكعب وهم عالمون بكذبه فيما يدعي ؟ هذا مما لا يكون، فكان هذا من أوضح الدلائل على ثبوت ذكره، والبشارة به في الكتب المتقدمة، وروي أحاديث كثيرة عن العلماء بالكتب المتقدمة في وجه ذكره فيها أعرضنا عن ذلك مخافة التطويل، وكذا وجد ذكره في أخبار الفرس ومنامات لهم أنذروا فيها بزوال ملكهم على يده، وكانوا يخافون ذلك وكذا في سير ملوك اليمن وغيرهم حتى حكوا في حكاية فيها طول عن تبع بن حسان بن تبع أنه قال في النبي عليه السلام: شهدت على أحمد أنه رسول من الله باري النسم فلو مد عمري إلى عمره لكنت وزيرًا له وابن عم وقصة سيف بن ذي يزن مع عبد المطلب مشهورة لا خفاء بها على من له أدنى علم بالتواريخ وسير الملوك، والله الهادي.
They will claim for the Messiah what they claimed. Among them are many phrases in the Gospel with the name Paraclete, from that the Paraclete is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends, that is, in my name he will teach you everything. The scholars mentioned in their books these phrases and many things from the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, including mention of him, mention of his companions, mention of Mecca, the Kaaba, the Sanctuary, the Stone, and other things. The People of the Two Books do not deny the establishment of that, except that they distort words from their places and divert all that with repugnant corrupt interpretations to other than what is intended. The imams of the people of kalam have mentioned that and invalidated their corrupt interpretations, and I refrained from mentioning that for fear of length, and sufficed from all that with a rational argument against which opponents have no objection and from which they have no separation, which is that Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their books and that he is given glad tidings upon the tongue of the Messiah, as God Almighty mentioned in His Book with His saying: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel,' and He Almighty said as a report about Jesus, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, I am the Messenger of God to you, confirming what came before me of the Torah and giving glad tidings of a Messenger who will come after me, whose name is Ahmad.' And He Almighty said: 'O People of the Scripture, why do you disbelieve in the signs of God while you witness?' 'O People of the Scripture, why do you mix the truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know?' And He said: 'Those to whom We gave the Scripture recognize him as they recognize their own sons.' And there are many verses whose enumeration would be long. And he used to call them to follow him and believe him, and he established for the correctness of his claim sufficient proofs that cut off the excuses of the deniers. So how could he argue against them with falsehood and refer that to what is with them and in their hands, and say: 'The sign of my authenticity and the proof of my truthfulness is that you find me written' while he knows that they will not find him, and he knows that that would increase them in aversion and distance from what he calls them to? And he was independent of that by the proofs he established. Would a madman do that? Let alone one whose wisdom covered the earth, and surpassed, according to the claim of the opponents, all the people of the earth in cunning and intelligence, and excelled all the eloquent in eloquence and fluency? And did not surrender, while the case is as they claimed, from his lie in his claim of the existence of his mention and glad tidings in the previous books - did any of their scholars and rabbis such as Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b, while they knew his lie in what he claims, surrender? This is something that cannot be. So this is among the clearest proofs for the establishment of his mention and glad tidings in the previous books. And many hadiths were reported from the scholars of the previous books regarding the manner of his mention in them; we refrained from that for fear of length. Likewise, his mention was found in the reports of the Persians and in their dreams in which they were warned of the removal of their kingdom at his hand, and they used to fear that. Likewise, in the biographies of the kings of Yemen and others, until they narrated in a lengthy story about Tubba' ibn Hassan ibn Tubba' that he said about the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'I testified that Ahmad is a messenger from God, the Creator of souls. If my lifetime extended to his lifetime, I would be a minister for him and a cousin.' And the story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan with Abd al-Muttalib is famous, not hidden from anyone who has the slightest knowledge of histories and biographies of kings. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 733

Commentary
This passage provides two interconnected proofs for the prophethood of Muhammad: first, the existence of his mention and glad tidings in earlier scriptures (particularly the Gospel), and second, a rational argument that he could not have falsely claimed such mention given his wisdom and the testimony of knowledgeable converts. The passage begins by noting specific phrases in the Gospel using the name 'Paraclete' (Faraqlit) identified as the Spirit of Truth. Scholars have recorded these and other details about the Prophet, his companions, and sacred places in earlier books. Nasafi acknowledges that the People of the Book do not deny these texts exist, but they distort their interpretation. He then offers a concise rational argument: the Prophet Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their scriptures and that Jesus gave tidings of him. If this were false, the Jewish and Christian scholars would have immediately exposed him, especially since he challenged them to verify it. But the Prophet was known for his wisdom and eloquence; even his opponents acknowledged his intelligence. It would be irrational for a wise person to make a claim easily disproved. Furthermore, many learned rabbis and priests like Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b converted after examining the scriptures, fully aware of their contents. If the claim were false, they would not have believed. Nasafi then extends the evidence to mentions in Persian and Yemeni traditions, citing Tubba' and Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan. The argument is that the widespread attestation of the Prophet's coming across multiple cultures and eras confirms the truth of his prophethood.

Key Terms
فارقليط
البشارة
الكتب المتقدمة
المعقول
الدلائل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof relies only on textual references from scriptures.
Correction: It combines scriptural testimony with a rational argument from the Prophet's integrity and the consensus of converts, as well as historical evidence from other cultures.

Checkpoint
What is the central rational argument Nasafi uses to prove the Prophet's mention in earlier scriptures?
A) The Prophet performed miracles that proved his truthfulness.
B) The Prophet’s claim of being mentioned, if false, would have been refuted by scholars, and many knowledgeable converts confirmed it.
C) The Torah and Gospel explicitly state his name many times.
D) The early Muslims accepted his claim without question.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's proof for prophethood combines scriptural references with a rational argument that the Prophet's claim could not be false given his wisdom and the conversion of knowledgeable scholars, further supported by historical attestations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet staked his entire mission on the claim that his coming was foretold. If you were in his place, would you have the same confidence? What does that reveal about the certitude of his knowledge and your own trust in divine promises?
?
Nasafi argues that no wise person would make a false claim that could be easily exposed. Think of a time you exaggerated or made a claim you knew might be disproven. How does the Prophet's integrity challenge your own honesty and consistency in matters of faith?
?
The learned converts surrendered to the truth despite knowing the scriptures well. Are you willing to submit to truth when it contradicts your preconceived notions or desires? What specifically holds you back from full submission?

Proof from Knowledge of Past Events
Nasafi introduces prophecy about past events as a proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate knowledge of past events serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge of unknowable past events is a divine sign of prophethood.

In this brief passage, Nasafi presents another rational proof of prophethood: the Prophet's knowledge of detailed past events that he could not have known through ordinary means. This knowledge, found in the Quranic accounts of previous prophets and nations, points to divine revelation and confirms his prophetic mission. The passage is incomplete, but its argument is clear and powerful.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice that the passage is a fragment but conveys a complete idea: the Prophet's knowledge of past events is proof.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the core argument is present.
2
Identify the type of knowledge
Nasafi specifies that the Prophet informed about 'specific past events' (al-ka’inat al-madiya al-juz’iyya). This is not general knowledge but precise details of past occurrences.
Examples include stories of the prophets of Israel and others.
3
Understand why this is a miracle
Reflect on why accurate knowledge of the past, especially detailed events from other nations, could not have been acquired naturally. The Prophet was unlettered and had no access to these accounts. This makes his knowledge a divine miracle (mu‘jiza).
4
Connect to the proof of prophethood
Consider how this knowledge serves as evidence that the Prophet is truly sent by God. Such knowledge is beyond human capacity, so it must come from revelation, confirming prophethood.

Source Text

علمه بما حدث في الماضي دليل على نبوته]: وأما ما هو راجع إلى إخباره عن الكائنات الماضية الجزئية فيما تضمن الكتاب من أخبار أنبياء بني إسرائيل وغيرهم مما لم يكن علم شيء من ذلك عند

Commentary
This brief passage introduces another proof of prophethood: the Prophet's accurate knowledge of detailed past events. Nasafi states that the Prophet informed about specific occurrences from the past, such as stories of the prophets of Israel and other nations, which he had no natural means of knowing. This knowledge, being beyond human acquisition, serves as a miracle (mu‘jiza) confirming his prophethood. The passage is incomplete, but the argument is clear: the report of the Quran about past events that were unknown to the people of that time is a divine sign. This is a standard kalam argument that the Prophet's knowledge of unseen past events (al-akhbar ‘an al-ghayb al-madi) constitutes a proof.

Prophecies of Future Events in the Quran as Proof of Prophethood (Part 1)
Nasafi introduces the proof from future prophecies and gives three Quranic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quranic prophecies of future events as a proof of the Prophet's prophethood, and you will be able to identify the three examples he provides from the Quran.

Core Idea
The Quran's accurate predictions of future events prove it is from Allah and confirms Muhammad's prophethood.

Nasafi presents another compelling proof of prophethood: the Quran's predictions of future events that came true exactly as foretold. He argues that such knowledge of the unseen could only come from Allah, and the Prophet's accurate reports demonstrate divine revelation. This lesson introduces the proof and examines three specific Quranic examples that were fulfilled in history.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and the literal translation. Notice how Nasafi first establishes the context of the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen coming from Allah.
Pay attention to the logical flow from general proof to specific examples.
2
Identify the two types of future prophecies
Nasafi divides prophecies into those in the Quran and those in hadith. For this lesson, focus on the Quranic examples.
The hadith examples are left for a later discussion.
3
Examine the first example: defeat at Badr
The verse 'سَيُهْزَمُ الْجَمْعُ وَيُوَلُّونَ الدُّبُرَ' (Quran 54:45) was revealed in Mecca and predicted the defeat of the polytheists at Badr. This was fulfilled exactly as stated.
Note the use of the future tense particle 'س' to indicate pure future.
4
Examine the second and third examples
The second example is the promise of one of the two parties (Quran 8:7), which referred to the army, not the caravan. The third is the call to fight a people of great might (Quran 48:16), interpreted as Banu Hanifa or Persians, fulfilled by Abu Bakr and Umar.
These examples show specificity and exact fulfillment.
5
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider how these public, specific predictions that came true exactly as foretold serve as a clear sign that the Quran is from Allah and Muhammad is His Prophet.
This proof is part of a larger argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The people of his town, and he did not go to anyone who had knowledge of that, and he informed in the manner that the Jewish rabbis and Christian scholars had learned, without increase or decrease, and he learned that from people like him among the illiterates who had not read the previous books nor taken that from their scholars and rabbis. This is from the door of knowledge of the unseen, which is not known except by Allah. So when he knew it, along with what we have explained of his condition, it indicates that he knew it by Allah's informing him. This is clear, praise be to Allah. His informing about what occurs in the future is a proof of his prophethood. As for what relates to his informing about future events, it is of two types: one is what is found in the Book, and the other is what is found in the hadith. As for what is in the Book, it is like His saying, exalted: 'The hosts will be defeated and they will turn their backs.' And the surah is Meccan, meaning thereby the polytheists on the day of Badr, and it was just as he informed. There is no doubt that it is an inform about what will be in the future, indicated by the letter sin which is placed for pure future tense and cutting off the possibility of the present tense for which the form is placed. And His saying, exalted: 'And when Allah promised you one of the two parties that it would be yours,' and it was for them, and it was the army, not the caravan. And His saying, exalted: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins: You will be called to a people of great might,' and they were called. Because what is meant by 'a people of great might' according to some is Banu Hanifa, and Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) called to fight them. And according to some, what is meant by that is the people of Persia, and Umar ibn al-Khattab called to that. And in the verse there is indication of the caliphates of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them), which we will explain when we reach the establishment of the imamate, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 735

Commentary
This passage is a proof for prophethood based on prophecies of future events. It begins by explaining that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen, like the knowledge of the People of the Book, came from Allah. Then it states that his informing about future events is a proof. The author divides such prophecies into two types: those in the Quran and those in the hadith. He then gives three examples from the Quran: 1) The verse 'The hosts will be defeated and they will turn their backs' (Quran 54:45) predicted the defeat of the polytheists at Badr, and it was fulfilled; 2) The verse 'And when Allah promised you one of the two parties that it would be yours' (Quran 8:7) referred to the army, not the caravan, and it was fulfilled; 3) The verse 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins: You will be called to a people of great might' (Quran 48:16) was interpreted as either Banu Hanifa (fought by Abu Bakr) or the Persians (fought by Umar), indicating the caliphates of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali. The author notes that this also supports the imamate, which will be discussed later.

Misconception: The Quran's predictions were vague or coincidental.
Correction: Nasafi emphasizes that these prophecies were specific (e.g., the defeat at Badr, the army not the caravan) and were fulfilled exactly as stated, indicating divine knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi demonstrates that the Quran's precise predictions of future events, such as the defeat at Badr and the call to fight Banu Hanifa or Persians, serve as clear proof that the Quran is from Allah and Muhammad is His Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran’s predictions about the future were so precise and fulfilled exactly as described, what does that say about your certainty that every promise Allah has made to you—in this life or the next—will come true? Are you living with that same level of certainty, or are you hedging your bets?
?
The Prophet ﷺ conveyed these prophecies without any formal education, relying solely on revelation. When you read about events foretold 1400 years ago that came true, does your heart submit fully to the truth of his message, or do you find yourself making excuses to keep a safe distance? What would it cost you to surrender completely?
?
The verse about 'a people of great might' was interpreted as both Banu Hanifa and the Persians, and both were fought by the righteous caliphs. This shows that the Quran's words have layers of meaning and were fulfilled in multiple ways. How does this humble your assumption that you have fully understood any single verse of the Quran? Are you willing to remain a student of the Book for life, never claiming to have mastered it?

Prophecies of the Romans and Future Conquests
Nasafi presents two Quranic prophecies: Romans and future conquests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two Quranic prophecies—the Roman victory after defeat and the conquests of Persia and Mecca—were historically fulfilled and serve as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled predictions confirm the Prophet's truthfulness.

Imam al-Nasafi continues his argument from prophecy by presenting two more examples from the Quran. The first is the surprising prediction that the Romans would be victorious after being defeated, which came true. The second is the verse about showing signs in the horizons and within themselves, interpreted by scholars as the conquests of Persia and Mecca. Both were fulfilled exactly as foretold.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation side by side. Notice how each prophecy is introduced with 'وكقوله تعالى' and ends with 'وكان كما أخبر'.
2
Identify the two prophecies
Find the first prophecy about the Romans (Surah Ar-Rum) and the second about signs in horizons and self (Surah Fussilat). Note the specific predictions.
3
Understand the interpretation
For the second prophecy, note that the verse is interpreted as future conquests rather than general signs of creation. The author cites the tafsir tradition.
4
Reflect on the argument
Ask: How do these fulfilled prophecies prove that Muhammad is a true prophet? Consider that only Allah knows the unseen future.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكقوله تعالى: ( الم ٥ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ والمراد منه معنى في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين، وقد أراهم الآيات الدالة على حدوثهم وثبوت الصانع الحكيم لهم في أنفسهم وفي الآفاق، فلم تكن الآية منصرفة إلى ذلك، وكان المراد ما قال أهل التأويل أن المراد بالآيات في الآفاق فتح الفرس، وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة، وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى لرسوله: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ أي مكة، وقد رد إليها. وكقوله تعالى: هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وقد أظهره. وكقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنْكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، والمراد من ذلك الصحابة بدلالة قوله تعالى: وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام وقبل الهجرة وقد استخلفهم، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود: قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِنْ زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِنْ دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني.
And like His saying, exalted: 'Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will be victorious' and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted: 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' and what is meant by it is a future meaning, indicated by the letter sin. And He showed them the signs indicating their origination and the establishment of the Wise Maker for them within themselves and in the horizons. So the verse was not referring to that, and what was meant was what the people of tafsir said: that what is meant by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and within themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted, to His Messenger: 'Indeed, He who imposed the Quran upon you will surely return you to a place of return' meaning Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His saying, exalted: 'It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to manifest it over all religion' and He manifested it. And like His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth' the verse, and what is meant by that are the Companions, indicated by His saying, exalted: 'and He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security' and they were the fearful ones in early Islam and before the Hijra, and He gave them succession. And in the verse there is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overpowered. And like His saying, exalted, concerning the Jews: 'Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah to the exclusion of the people' until He said: 'and they will not wish for it ever' and it was as he informed, and none of them wished for death. And in the verse there is evidence that they knew the truth of his message, and they found his mention in their books, where they did not dare to wish for death.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage continues the proof from future prophecies by giving more Quranic examples. The first example is the prophecy of the Romans' defeat and subsequent victory (Quran 30:1-3), which was fulfilled. The second is the verse 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' (Quran 41:53), interpreted by scholars as the conquest of Persia (horizons) and the conquest of Mecca (within themselves), and it was fulfilled. The third is the promise to return to Mecca (Quran 28:85), which was fulfilled when the Prophet conquered Mecca. The fourth is the promise that Islam would prevail over all religions (Quran 61:9), which was fulfilled. The fifth is the promise of succession and security for the believers (Quran 24:55), which was fulfilled with the caliphates, especially Abu Bakr's. The sixth is regarding the Jews: the verse challenging them to wish for death if they claim to be Allah's favorites (Quran 62:6-7); they never wished for death, proving they knew Muhammad was true, as they had his description in their scriptures.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the verse is about future prophecies, as indicated by the future tense, and scholars interpret it as the conquests of Persia and Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The fulfillment of Quranic prophecies about the Romans and future conquests demonstrates that the Quran's knowledge of the unseen comes from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quran promised the Romans victory after defeat, and it happened. In your own life, what situation feels like a defeat right now? Are you willing to trust that Allah's promise of victory or relief is as certain as this prophecy? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that?
?
The signs in the horizons and within yourself include future victories. But the verse also says 'We will show them Our signs.' Have you seen Allah's signs in your own life and surroundings? What is one sign you have witnessed that left no doubt in your heart? If you cannot think of any, does that mean you have not been looking? Today, commit to noticing one sign of Allah's power or mercy before you sleep.
?
The conquest of Mecca was foretold before it happened. Allah knows the outcome of every struggle. When you strive for something good, do you worry about the result as if Allah does not know? Or do you work with certainty that the end is already written and good? Put your worry aside and name one struggle you will hand over to Allah's knowledge today.

Prophecies of Return to Mecca and Islam's Prevalence
Nasafi presents two prophecies: return to Mecca and Islam's prevalence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecies of the Prophet's return to Mecca and Islam's dominance over all religions were fulfilled and serve as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Divine promises about the Prophet's return and Islam's victory came true.

This passage presents two more Quranic prophecies: the promise that the Prophet would return to Mecca (his birthplace) after being forced to leave, and the promise that Islam would be made prevalent over all religions. Both were fulfilled exactly as foretold, providing clear evidence of the truth of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two prophecies introduced with 'وكقوله تعالى'.
2
Identify the prophecies
The first is from Surah Al-Qasas (28:85) about returning to 'ma'ad' (Mecca). The second is from Surah As-Saff (61:9) about manifesting Islam over all religions.
3
Confirm the fulfillments
Recall that the Prophet indeed returned to Mecca in the year of the conquest (8 AH) and that Islam spread rapidly, becoming dominant over other religions in Arabia and beyond.
4
Appreciate the argument
These predictions were made at a time when the Prophet was weak and outnumbered. Their fulfillment shows divine support.

وكقوله تعالى: ( الم ٥ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ والمراد منه معنى في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين، وقد أراهم الآيات الدالة على حدوثهم وثبوت الصانع الحكيم لهم في أنفسهم وفي الآفاق، فلم تكن الآية منصرفة إلى ذلك، وكان المراد ما قال أهل التأويل أن المراد بالآيات في الآفاق فتح الفرس، وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة، وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى لرسوله: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ أي مكة، وقد رد إليها. وكقوله تعالى: هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وقد أظهره. وكقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنْكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، والمراد من ذلك الصحابة بدلالة قوله تعالى: وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام وقبل الهجرة وقد استخلفهم، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود: قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِنْ زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِنْ دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني.
And like His saying, exalted: 'Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will be victorious' and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted: 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' and what is meant by it is a future meaning, indicated by the letter sin. And He showed them the signs indicating their origination and the establishment of the Wise Maker for them within themselves and in the horizons. So the verse was not referring to that, and what was meant was what the people of tafsir said: that what is meant by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and within themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted, to His Messenger: 'Indeed, He who imposed the Quran upon you will surely return you to a place of return' meaning Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His saying, exalted: 'It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to manifest it over all religion' and He manifested it. And like His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth' the verse, and what is meant by that are the Companions, indicated by His saying, exalted: 'and He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security' and they were the fearful ones in early Islam and before the Hijra, and He gave them succession. And in the verse there is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overpowered. And like His saying, exalted, concerning the Jews: 'Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah to the exclusion of the people' until He said: 'and they will not wish for it ever' and it was as he informed, and none of them wished for death. And in the verse there is evidence that they knew the truth of his message, and they found his mention in their books, where they did not dare to wish for death.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage continues the proof from future prophecies by giving more Quranic examples. The first example is the prophecy of the Romans' defeat and subsequent victory (Quran 30:1-3), which was fulfilled. The second is the verse 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' (Quran 41:53), interpreted by scholars as the conquest of Persia (horizons) and the conquest of Mecca (within themselves), and it was fulfilled. The third is the promise to return to Mecca (Quran 28:85), which was fulfilled when the Prophet conquered Mecca. The fourth is the promise that Islam would prevail over all religions (Quran 61:9), which was fulfilled. The fifth is the promise of succession and security for the believers (Quran 24:55), which was fulfilled with the caliphates, especially Abu Bakr's. The sixth is regarding the Jews: the verse challenging them to wish for death if they claim to be Allah's favorites (Quran 62:6-7); they never wished for death, proving they knew Muhammad was true, as they had his description in their scriptures.

قرآن
معاد
أظهر
الدين
كله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which city is referred to as 'مَعَادٍ' in the prophecy about returning?
A) Medina
B) Jerusalem
C) Mecca
D) Ta'if

Key Takeaway
The fulfillment of the prophecies of return to Mecca and Islam's prevalence confirms that the Quran is from Allah and Muhammad is His true messenger.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's promises are fulfilled without fail, what one area of your life would change most dramatically? What is holding you back from acting on that belief today?
?
The Prophet was promised return to Mecca when he was at his weakest. Think of a situation where you feel powerless. Are you waiting for Allah's promise to materialize, or have you lost hope? What keeps you from trusting His word completely?
?
Islam's prevalence over all religions is a proven fact of history. Yet your own adherence may waver. What does your daily prioritization say about your conviction that this religion will ultimately triumph?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Prophecies of Succession and the Jews' Death Wish
Nasafi presents prophecies of succession and Jewish death wish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecies of caliphate succession for the believers and the Jews' inability to wish for death serve as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Future events about the community and the Jews' disbelief were foretold and fulfilled.

In this final part, Imam al-Nasafi presents two more powerful prophecies. The first is the promise of succession and security for the believers, which was fulfilled with the caliphate of Abu Bakr and the expansion of Islam. The second is the challenge to the Jews to wish for death if they are Allah's favorites, which they never did, proving their knowledge of the Prophet's truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two separate prophecies: one about succession, one about the Jews.
2
Understand the succession prophecy
The verse (Quran 24:55) promises that believers will be made successors on earth and will have security. The author specifies this refers to the Companions and particularly to the caliphate of Abu Bakr.
The phrase 'لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا' argues that Abu Bakr was not overpowered, establishing his legitimate caliphate.
3
Reflect on the Jewish prophecy
The verse (Quran 62:6-7) challenges Jews to wish for death if they are Allah's favorites, but they never do. This shows they knew Muhammad was true and feared judgment.
4
Connect to the overall proof
Both prophecies were fulfilled in history and could not have been known by human guessing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكقوله تعالى: ( الم ٥ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ والمراد منه معنى في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين، وقد أراهم الآيات الدالة على حدوثهم وثبوت الصانع الحكيم لهم في أنفسهم وفي الآفاق، فلم تكن الآية منصرفة إلى ذلك، وكان المراد ما قال أهل التأويل أن المراد بالآيات في الآفاق فتح الفرس، وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة، وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى لرسوله: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ أي مكة، وقد رد إليها. وكقوله تعالى: هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وقد أظهره. وكقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنْكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، والمراد من ذلك الصحابة بدلالة قوله تعالى: وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام وقبل الهجرة وقد استخلفهم، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود: قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِنْ زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِنْ دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني.

Commentary
This passage continues the proof from future prophecies by giving more Quranic examples. The first example is the prophecy of the Romans' defeat and subsequent victory (Quran 30:1-3), which was fulfilled. The second is the verse 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' (Quran 41:53), interpreted by scholars as the conquest of Persia (horizons) and the conquest of Mecca (within themselves), and it was fulfilled. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Jews simply ignored the challenge, but the author argues their failure itself is evidence of their knowledge.
Correction: The passage states that the Jews did not dare to wish for death because they knew the Prophet's truth from their scriptures, making their inaction a fulfillment of the prophecy.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Jews' failure to wish for death indicate?
A) They were not serious about their claim
B) They knew Muhammad was a true prophet
C) They did not read the Quran
D) They preferred life over death

Key Takeaway
The precise fulfillment of prophecies about succession and the Jews' behavior demonstrates the divine origin of Islam and the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Jews knew the truth of Muhammad's prophethood from their scriptures but did not act. Where in your own life do you know something is true from Allah but hesitate to embrace it fully? What fear drives that hesitation, and what would it cost you to act on that truth today?
?
The Companions moved from fear to security through trust in Allah's promise. In what area of your life are you still living in fear—whether of failure, people, or the future—instead of trusting Allah's guarantee of succession and security? What is one concrete step you can take this week to replace that fear with faith?
?
If Allah challenged you to wish for death to prove your sincerity, would you dare? What does your honest answer reveal about the strength of your certainty in His promise? How can you strengthen that certainty starting today?
