Examples of the Prophet's Predictions of the Unseen
Al-Nasafi lists examples of the Prophet's predictions of the unseen during his lifetime.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate predictions of future events serve as evidence of his prophethood, through several historical examples.

Core Idea
The Prophet's predictions always came true, proving divine knowledge.

Al-Nasafi presents a series of incidents from the Prophet's life where he accurately foretold future events. These examples demonstrate that his knowledge was not ordinary but came from Allah, distinguishing him from false prophets and soothsayers. Let's examine each case closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the examples of the Prophet's predictions
Read through each example: the night journey news, the lost camel, Ukaydir hunting cows, the secret wealth of al-Abbas, and the exposure of hypocrites' thoughts.
Notice how each prediction was verified exactly as told.
2
Identify the common pattern
In each case, the Prophet revealed specific information about the unseen that no one could know normally, and the events unfolded exactly as he said.
This consistency is key to proving divine origin.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why al-Nasafi includes multiple examples. They build a cumulative argument that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen was ongoing and reliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما . ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون : هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: "أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر" فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: "افد نفسك وابني أخيك" يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارثة- فإنك ذو مال فقال : لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا، ولعبد الله كذا، ولفلان كذا ؟ فقال العباس والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم ، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله ، والله الموفق . ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين الذين يضل صدقهم في كذبهم وحقهم في باطلهم على أن حالته كانت تخالف حالة الكهنة في طهارته وطيبه واشتغاله بالطاعات والعبادات. وتقدر أولئك وتنجسهم وتقربهم إلى الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة ، وكذا كانت أخباره صادرة عنه عن طريق الغيب الذي أعلمه الله تعالى من غير الاشتغال بالنظر في النجوم والتأمل في الطالع والارتفاع وتعرف ذلك من قبل الريح والإسطرلاب وغير ذلك من خلاف ما يفعله المنجمة، فكان ذلك من باب نقض العادة كإلانة الحديد واتخاذ الدروع بلا آلات ولا استعمال النار.
Among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as [he said]. And among that is that a she-camel of his, peace be upon him, was lost, so he began asking people about it, and the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you the news of heaven while he does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and thanked Him, and narrated their words, then said: 'I know only what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such a valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people rushed and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'You will come to him and find him hunting cows' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your two nephews' meaning Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth that you left in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl while no one else was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then so-and-so for al-Fadl, so-and-so for Abdullah, and so-and-so for so-and-so?' Al-Abbas said: 'By Him Who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knew this besides me. You are indeed the Messenger of God.' And he and Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is that he used to inform the people of hypocrisy about what they said among themselves and plotted of speech that does not please [God], until they, due to their obstinacy, feared that a surah would be revealed telling them what was in their hearts. And similar examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it. And God is the Granter of success. Then indeed all the reports he gave of future events came out as he reported without any possibility of falsehood or error in any of that, unlike the reports of soothsayers and astrologers whose truth is mixed with falsehood and whose correctness is mixed with error, while his state was contrary to the state of soothsayers in his purity, goodness, and engagement in acts of obedience and worship, and their impurity, defilement, and closeness to devils and evil spirits. Likewise, his reports came from him through the unseen which God Almighty taught him, without engaging in observation of stars, contemplation of horoscopes and ascendants, and knowing that by means of wind and astrolabe and other things contrary to what astrologers do. Thus it was a breach of [natural] custom, like softening iron and making coats of mail without tools or use of fire.
Source pages p. 739

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof of prophethood through predictions of the unseen. The author, al-Nasafi, provides several concrete examples from the Prophet's life where he accurately foretold events, including the location of a lost camel, the hunting habits of a king, a secret wealth transfer, and the secret thoughts of hypocrites. He concludes that all such predictions came true without exception. He then contrasts this with the unreliable reports of soothsayers (kuhhan) and astrologers (munajjimun), who sometimes speak truth but are often wrong. The Prophet's state of purity and devotion also differs from theirs, as they seek closeness to devils. Moreover, the Prophet received knowledge directly from God through revelation, not through astrological methods. Therefore, these predictions are miraculous breaches of natural custom (kharq al-ada), like the softening of iron for David.

Key Terms
نبوة
غيب
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's knowledge of the unseen was occasional and not always accurate.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows through multiple examples that his predictions always came true exactly as stated, with no errors.

Checkpoint

A) He denied it and continued to reject Islam.
B) He was amazed and immediately accepted Islam.
C) He asked for proof and then accepted.
D) He remained silent.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate and repeated predictions of the unseen prove that his knowledge came from Allah, not from human means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The story of al-Abbas shows that the Prophet knew his secret wealth. When you hide things from your family or community, do you truly believe that Allah will expose them just as He exposed al-Abbas? How should this change your attitude towards honesty?
?
The hypocrites feared that a surah would be revealed exposing what was in their hearts. Are there thoughts or intentions in your heart that you would be ashamed if Allah revealed? What are you doing to purify them?
?
When the Prophet did not know where his she-camel was, the hypocrites mocked him. Have you ever doubted the Prophet's knowledge when something didn't happen as you expected? How does this lesson affirm that his knowledge is from Allah alone?

How Prophetic Knowledge Differs from Soothsayers and Astrologers
Al-Nasafi contrasts the Prophet's revelations with soothsayers and astrologers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen differs fundamentally from that of soothsayers and astrologers, and why his predictions are considered miracles.

Core Idea
Prophetic knowledge is pure and perfect, unlike the mixed and impure reports of soothsayers.

After presenting examples of the Prophet's accurate predictions, al-Nasafi contrasts them with the predictions of soothsayers (kuhhan) and astrologers (munajjimun). He highlights the absolute reliability of the Prophet's reports compared to the mixed truth and falsehood of others, and the purity of his character versus their impurity. This distinction elevates the Prophet's predictions to the level of miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the contrast passage
Read the portion starting from 'Then indeed all the reports...' and note the key points of contrast: truthfulness, purity, and method of knowledge.
2
Understand the difference in reliability
Al-Nasafi states that all of the Prophet's future reports came true without any falsehood, unlike soothsayers whose truth is mixed with falsehood.
3
Understand the difference in character and method
The Prophet was pure and engaged in worship, while soothsayers were impure and sought devils. The Prophet received knowledge directly from Allah, not through stars or divination.
4
Connect to the concept of miracle (kharq al-ada)
This is described as a breach of natural custom, similar to the softening of iron for Prophet David. The perfect knowledge of the unseen is a supernatural event.

ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما . ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون : هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: "أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر" فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: "افد نفسك وابني أخيك" يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارثة- فإنك ذو مال فقال : لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا، ولعبد الله كذا، ولفلان كذا ؟ فقال العباس والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم ، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله ، والله الموفق . ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين الذين يضل صدقهم في كذبهم وحقهم في باطلهم على أن حالته كانت تخالف حالة الكهنة في طهارته وطيبه واشتغاله بالطاعات والعبادات. وتقدر أولئك وتنجسهم وتقربهم إلى الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة ، وكذا كانت أخباره صادرة عنه عن طريق الغيب الذي أعلمه الله تعالى من غير الاشتغال بالنظر في النجوم والتأمل في الطالع والارتفاع وتعرف ذلك من قبل الريح والإسطرلاب وغير ذلك من خلاف ما يفعله المنجمة، فكان ذلك من باب نقض العادة كإلانة الحديد واتخاذ الدروع بلا آلات ولا استعمال النار.
Among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as [he said]. And among that is that a she-camel of his, peace be upon him, was lost, so he began asking people about it, and the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you the news of heaven while he does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and thanked Him, and narrated their words, then said: 'I know only what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such a valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people rushed and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'You will come to him and find him hunting cows' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your two nephews' meaning Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth that you left in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl while no one else was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then so-and-so for al-Fadl, so-and-so for Abdullah, and so-and-so for so-and-so?' Al-Abbas said: 'By Him Who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knew this besides me. You are indeed the Messenger of God.' And he and Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is that he used to inform the people of hypocrisy about what they said among themselves and plotted of speech that does not please [God], until they, due to their obstinacy, feared that a surah would be revealed telling them what was in their hearts. And similar examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it. And God is the Granter of success. Then indeed all the reports he gave of future events came out as he reported without any possibility of falsehood or error in any of that, unlike the reports of soothsayers and astrologers whose truth is mixed with falsehood and whose correctness is mixed with error, while his state was contrary to the state of soothsayers in his purity, goodness, and engagement in acts of obedience and worship, and their impurity, defilement, and closeness to devils and evil spirits. Likewise, his reports came from him through the unseen which God Almighty taught him, without engaging in observation of stars, contemplation of horoscopes and ascendants, and knowing that by means of wind and astrolabe and other things contrary to what astrologers do. Thus it was a breach of [natural] custom, like softening iron and making coats of mail without tools or use of fire.
Source pages p. 739

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof of prophethood through predictions of the unseen. The author, al-Nasafi, provides several concrete examples from the Prophet's life where he accurately foretold events, including the location of a lost camel, the hunting habits of a king, a secret wealth transfer, and the secret thoughts of hypocrites. He concludes that all such predictions came true without exception. He then contrasts this with the unreliable reports of soothsayers (kuhhan) and astrologers (munajjimun), who sometimes speak truth but are often wrong. The Prophet's state of purity and devotion also differs from theirs, as they seek closeness to devils. Moreover, the Prophet received knowledge directly from God through revelation, not through astrological methods. Therefore, these predictions are miraculous breaches of natural custom (kharq al-ada), like the softening of iron for David.

Key Terms
كهانة
تنجيم
نقض العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's knowledge is similar to that of soothsayers because both claim to know the unseen.
Correction: The Prophet's knowledge is always true, comes from Allah, and is accompanied by purity, whereas soothsayers' knowledge is mixed with falsehood and comes from devils.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what is the source of the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen?
A) Observation of stars and planets.
B) Divine revelation from Allah.
C) Deduction from natural signs.
D) Conversations with jinn.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's predictions are a miracle because they are perfectly true, come from divine revelation, and are accompanied by a pure character, unlike the flawed reports of soothsayers and astrologers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever sought knowledge of the future from a horoscope, fortune-teller, or 'lucky charm'? What does this lesson reveal about the source and reliability of such knowledge, and how will you respond next time you are tempted?
?
The Prophet's purity and devotion were essential to his prophethood. Examine your own daily habits: are they drawing you closer to Allah and purity, or are you casually engaging in practices (even small ones) that resemble the soothsayers' reliance on created things? What specific change will you make today?
?
You have just learned that true knowledge of the unseen comes only from Allah, and that the Prophet's predictions were perfect miracles. Does your heart truly trust in Allah's decree and the Prophet's message, or do you still secretly rely on other sources for reassurance? What is one step you can take to strengthen your reliance on Allah alone?
